The League of Nations that Resolves Disputes?

Accepting the Anglo-Persian Oil Dispute Case

The British Empire is Impatient. The Persian Representative is Unable to Attend. Will Invoke the Precedent of the Liaoning Case to Send an Investigation Team. National News Agency, Geneva, 19th. Although the Persian representative strongly advocated for postponing the discussion to await the arrival of Persian experts, the League of Nations is expected to invoke the precedent of the Lytton investigation before the League of Nations Executive Council meets on Monday to discuss the case of the D'Arcy oil concession between Britain and Persia, and send a special investigation committee as an initial solution. Persia has stated that it is willing to provide various conveniences to the special investigation team, and before the case is resolved, it will respect the current situation.

Reuters, Geneva, 18th. British Foreign Secretary Simon is currently suffering from a cold in London and cannot go to Geneva. Therefore, when the League of Nations Executive Council handles the Anglo-Persian oil concession dispute tomorrow afternoon, the person representing Britain to present the case will be Mr. Malkin, Legal Advisor to the British Foreign Office. It is heard that the Persian government will not have a representative in attendance tomorrow, so this meeting will only be a formality.

National News Agency, Geneva, 19th. The League of Nations today released a document issued by Persia on the 17th, complaining that Britain is using intimidation and threats in the dispute with the Anglo-Persian Oil Company, but does not object to submitting it to the League of Nations Executive Council, only requesting the Executive Council to postpone detailed consideration of the case until the Persian experts arrive in Geneva. At the same time, the League of Nations also released a 30-page statement by Britain, accusing Persia of canceling the concession as a unilateral act of confiscation in violation of international conventions, and requested the League of Nations to take appropriate steps to maintain the status quo and prevent the interests of the Anglo-Persian Oil Company from being damaged during the Executive Council's consideration.

Reuters, Geneva, 19th. The British government submitted a statement this morning to the League of Nations Executive Council regarding the Persian government's cancellation of the Anglo-Persian Oil Company's D'Arcy oil concession, stating that Britain is extremely willing to resolve this dispute through a peaceful and fair agreement. However, the Persian government believes that this concession can be canceled by unilateral action, leading to a failure in negotiations. Therefore, it requests the Executive Council to take necessary steps to 1) maintain the status quo, and 2) prevent damage to the interests of the Anglo-Persian Oil Company while negotiations are not yet completed. The statement also stated that the British government is submitting this dispute to the Executive Council in its capacity as a government, not as a shareholder, to protect its nationals from damage to their interests due to another country's violation of international conventions. The original contract between the company had provisions for submitting disputes to arbitration, but Persia actually canceled this contract, although it indicated that it could grant the company a new concession in principle. The statement also stated that Britain sent a note to Persia on December 2, stating that the cancellation of the contract was an unacceptable action, and that the British government attached great importance to it and requested its immediate withdrawal. If Persia ultimately confiscates the company's assets, it will cause significant damage to the company and create an extremely serious incident. According to the contract, Persia should protect the company's assets, but Persia is not responsible for any losses to the company, so the British government is very concerned.

Establishment of the French Left-Wing Cabinet

Peng Gu Serves as Premier and Foreign Minister

Most Former Members Retained

Maintaining Previous Cabinet Policies

Socialist Party Refuses Cooperation Due to Political Differences

National News Agency, Paris, 18th: Peng Gu has formed the French cabinet. Peng himself will serve as Premier and Foreign Minister; Republican Democratic Socialist Party member and former Justice Minister Sérol will serve as Finance Minister; Radical Socialist Party member and former Premier Chautemps will serve as Interior Minister; Democratic Left-wing member and former Agriculture Minister Senator Queuille will serve as Justice Minister; Radical Socialist Party member and former Minister of Public Works Daladier will serve as Minister of War; Republican Left-wing member and former Premier Leygues will retain his position as Minister of the Navy; former Premier Painlevé will retain his position as Minister of Air; Democratic Left-wing member Sarraut will retain his position as Colonial Minister; Radical Socialist Party member Dali Mayo will retain his position as Minister of Labor; former Minister of Posts Bonner will serve as Minister of Public Works; Radical Left-wing member and former Minister of Air Eynac will serve as Minister of Posts and Telegraphs; Mayor of Le Havre, Méyer, will retain his position as Minister of Merchant Marine; former Minister of Posts Queuille will serve as Minister of Agriculture; the Minister of Budget has yet to be determined.

Havas, Paris, 18th: After the list of new cabinet members was announced to the press by the new Interior Minister Chautemps, the new Premier Peng Gu issued a declaration stating, "[The new cabinet is an extension of the Herriot cabinet, as can be seen from the list of new cabinet members. The policies of the new cabinet will be further demonstrated in the future.]"

Sérol's appointment as Finance Minister further demonstrates the government's desire to reveal the true state of finances to the people and to take necessary measures. The new cabinet will hold its first cabinet meeting at the Ministry of War tomorrow afternoon at 3:00 PM.

Havas, Paris, 18th: The Socialist Party's reasons for not wanting to cooperate with the Peng Gu cabinet are no more than the following: after lengthy discussions between the two sides, they failed to agree. The main points are: (1) Regarding the 40-hour work week system, Peng Gu said that it should be determined according to international plans and cannot be determined by France alone; (2) Regarding the national monopoly of the insurance industry, it is not appropriate to implement it at present due to psychological factors; (3) Regarding budget balance, a fair method should be used to require all classes of people to uniformly endure sacrifices; (4) Regarding the supervision of banks, Peng Gu advocated following the original conditions set by the Herriot cabinet; (5) Peng Gu believed that insurance for unemployment and agricultural disasters was too costly; (6) Peng Gu believed that national stability could not be guaranteed internationally by any means other than military preparations, so military spending could not be reduced for a single day. However, the term of military service, from one year to eight months, should be reviewed as soon as there is an opportunity. These are the points on which the Socialist Party and Peng Gu could not agree. However, although the Socialist Party will not participate in the Peng Gu cabinet, it is still willing to assist in Peng Gu's policies. The conditions for its assistance are the same as before for the Herriot cabinet. Therefore, those directly assisting the Peng Gu cabinet are the Radical Socialist Party, the French Socialist Party, and the Left-wing Radical Party. As for the Right-wing, the Republican Democratic Federation, and the Communist Party, they stand in opposition.

National News Agency, Paris, 19th: France's new Peng Gu cabinet is truly radical in nature. Among the seventeen cabinet members, twelve belong to the Radical Socialist Party. In addition, Peng Gu himself is non-partisan; Navy Minister Leygues has served in the naval departments of both left and right-wing cabinets and can be considered a naval expert, but he also belongs to the central left-wing; Finance Minister Sarraut is a former cabinet member of the Poincaré cabinet and is joining a left-wing cabinet for the first time, but he still belongs to the Republican Party; Minister of Posts Eynac is a radical left-wing member; Minister of Air Painlevé belongs to the Republican Socialist Party. Furthermore, judging from the backgrounds of the new cabinet members, no fewer than twelve are members of the bar association, which can be called a cabinet of lawyers. In addition, six have served as university professors, five as journalists, two as doctors, one as an agriculturalist, one as a civil servant, and one as a publisher. Among the new cabinet members, twelve have served in the old Herriot cabinet. However, there are also six ministers and vice-ministers who are serving in a cabinet position for the first time. As for those who have served multiple terms and can be called cabinet experts, in addition to Navy Minister Leygues, there are Agriculture Minister Queuille, Minister of Merchant Marine Méyer, and Minister of Air Painlevé, among others.

Peng Gu's Brief Biography

Good Friends with the Late Foreign Minister Briand

Creator of the "War Potential" Theory

Havas, Paris, 18th: The new Premier Peng Gu participated in a cabinet before the war and recently served as Minister of War in the Herriot cabinet. Although he has been in the cabinet twice, this is the first time he has served as Premier. Peng Gu is nearly sixty years old and was previously a lawyer in the criminal court, with a high reputation. His political life has been largely devoted to the Socialist Party. Last year, he left the party due to disagreements on the issue of arms reduction. Peng has been a member of the Paris Chamber of Deputies for a long time and was later elected as a Senator. After the establishment of the League of Nations, Peng Gu often assisted the French Premier in attending the League of Nations. In 1924, when Herriot advocated the "General Protocol for Arbitration, Security, and Disarmament" in Geneva, Peng Gu also participated in it. Later, when Briand shouldered important diplomatic responsibilities in Geneva, Peng's assistance was also significant. Peng and Briand were close friends. The concept of "war potential" is known throughout the world, and Peng Gu is the creator of this theory. Peng Gu created this theory while working on the Preparatory Commission for the Disarmament Conference. Peng Gu's so-called "war potential" means that when assessing a country's ability to wage war in peacetime, one should not only examine its existing military forces but also consider other factors, such as population productivity, industrial resources, etc. For example, a steel bell on a door may seem unrelated to war, but when war comes, it can be used to cast bullets. This is the so-called potential ability. After Briand's death, Peng Gu succeeded him as France's permanent representative to the League of Nations. Soon after, he was invited by Léry to join the cabinet as Minister of War. Peng has a pale face and no beard and often wears a black tie with white flowers. Because he resembles Robespierre during the French Revolution, he is called Robespierre by contemporaries. He is skilled in debate and speaks clearly. He has a long-standing reputation among international figures.

The Course of Cai Peishu's Arrest

(Nanjing) Cai Pei was released on the evening of the 17th with the help of Wu Zhihui and others. Cai stated the following: Sun Xiaotao, a female student at the Hangzhou Police Academy, sent a telegram to the Academic Affairs Office of Nanjing Cultural College three months ago, reporting on the activities in the school in coded language. The telegram was discovered and withheld by the authorities of the Police Academy. The school secretly reported it to the Military Affairs Commission, which ordered the special service group of the Police Department to investigate. Cai happened to be invited by Li Peitian, President of the Cultural College, to serve as the Director of Academic Affairs of the College in October. The Police Department did not investigate and mistakenly thought that the telegram sent by Sun Xiaotao was related to Cai, so they arrested him. In fact, Cai said that he took office as the Director of Academic Affairs in late October, and the telegram sent by Sun Xiaotao was still in September. Furthermore, Sun Xiaotao had previously studied at the Cultural College, but after the summer vacation this year, she was admitted to the Hangzhou Police Academy, which was more than three months after Cai arrived at the Cultural College. Therefore, Cai did not know Sun Xiaotao. After Cai was wronged, he resigned from both the position of Director of Academic Affairs and School Board Member of the Cultural College (19th Special Dispatch).

Guangdong Province Plans to Establish Wengjiang Hydroelectric Plant

The Expenses Will Be at Least Six Million US Dollars; the Entire Project Will Take Approximately Six Years to Complete

Guangzhou Correspondence: The Beijiang River in Guangdong meanders through the mountains, and the power of the waterfalls between the valleys is extraordinarily great. The authorities had long considered building a hydroelectric plant. It was not until recently that a plan was drafted and submitted to the Southwest Political Committee for review by members Lin Yungai and Liu Jiwen. The review has now been completed and submitted to the Technical Committee of the Construction Department for design and implementation. The preparation plan is as follows: The Wengjiang River is a tributary of the Beijiang River, joining the Beijiang in Yingde. The hydroelectric plant is planned to build a dam near the Shuikou area of ​​Wengyuan County, approximately 90 feet high. A power plant will be built under the dam, using 66,000 volts to transmit electricity to Guangzhou and other places. According to engineers' estimates, the water volume of the Wengjiang River during the dry season is 2,500 cubic feet per second. If the water storage capacity upstream of the dam is utilized, 3,000 cubic feet per second can be obtained during the dry season, and 5,000 cubic feet per second can be obtained during normal times. Building a 90-foot dam will result in an effective head of 80 feet, yielding 16,400 horsepower during the dry season and 14,784 kilowatts of electricity. During normal times, 36,666 horsepower can be obtained, yielding 20,536 kilowatts of electricity. As for the construction engineering: 1) Water source: Utilize the stream valley upstream of the dam, approximately 50 zhang long. 2) Water intake: Use a direct internal diameter of 20-foot tunnel to divert water. 3) Underground power plant: Use reinforced concrete to build a water pressure chamber 20 feet wide and 150 feet long, with a sand and mud discharge outlet at one end. 4) Dam: The upper part is 20 feet thick, the base is 80 feet thick, 110 feet high, and 500 feet long, all made of concrete. 5) The water immersion area upstream of the dam will occupy approximately 200 mu of paddy fields, 200 mu of pine forests, and approximately 300 mu of forests, affecting approximately 30 households, with losses of no more than 5,000 yuan. The power plant will be built on both banks of the dam, approximately 500 feet away from the dam. The generators will use five machines with a capacity of 1,000 kilowatts each. The electricity generated by the generators, approximately 6,600 volts, will be sent to a special high-voltage room, transformed into 66,000 volts via seven single-phase step-up transformers with 3,500 kilowatts, and then transmitted 13 miles to Guangzhou, where seven single-phase step-down transformers will reduce it to 3,300 volts. As for the start-up costs, equipment costs, and capital, approximately 6 million US dollars will be required. However, according to estimates by the Canadian Fellisby Company, 10 million US dollars will be required. The preparation engineering is divided into four phases. The first phase is limited to three months for surveying. The second phase involves designing the dam site and the machinery and equipment for the entire plant. The third phase involves sending letters to factories in various countries for bidding. If it is not completed within a year, an engineering office will be established publicly for design and construction, which will take approximately one year to complete. The fourth phase involves supervising various constructions and installing machinery, which will take four years. The entire project is expected to be fully completed in six years. (December 14th)

Hunan Province Divides Areas to Inspect Opium Prohibition

The Entire Province Is Divided into Fifteen Districts, with Special Commissioners Assigned to Assist in the Prohibition Policy

Changsha Correspondence: Since the establishment of the Opium Prohibition Committee in Hunan Province, opium dens in Changsha City have been closed separately, and native opium establishments have also been closed in accordance with the order. All unsold special goods (i.e., opium) are stored in a transfer station and twelve warehouses, responsible for transportation and sales. As for the counties that have always grown opium, the military and political leaders of the respective regions are strictly ordered to eliminate them within a time limit. The Chen Quzhen unit stationed in western Hunan is given a subsidy of 40,000 yuan per month by the provincial government to abolish the opium seedling tax in order to implement the prohibition of planting. All opium offenders caught in the counties are sentenced to imprisonment and no longer released on fines. Therefore, although the handling has only been two months, the atmosphere in all areas has changed. According to reports, thirty-seven counties, including Pingjiang, Zixing, Xiangtan, Xiangxiang, and Hengyang, have established opium abstinence centers. Thirty-one counties, including Yongming, Ningyuan, Hengshan, Changning, Hanshou, and Jiahe, have no opium seedlings or have been eradicated. The remaining counties are currently conducting separate surveys and eradications. The committee recently learned that opium prohibition inspectors dispatched by the Third Provincial Bandit Suppression Headquarters will soon come to Hunan to investigate and determine the opium prohibition situation in each county and whether opium seedlings have been completely eliminated. It is necessary to conduct an on-site inspection in advance to avoid delays. Therefore, the entire province is divided into fifteen districts, with one inspector and one secretary assigned to each district to be responsible for supervision in the respective areas. The divided areas and the responsibilities of the inspectors are as follows:

Areas

(First District) Inspector Liao Hequn, Secretary Liao Bingkun (covering six counties: Changsha, Xiangyin, Yueyang, Linxiang, Pingjiang, and Liuyang).

(Second District) Inspector Liu Zhu'an, Secretary Wu Songtao, covering six counties: Yuanjiang, Yiyang, Ningxiang, Xiangtan, Xiangxiang, and Hengshan. (Third District) Inspector Zhou Dachun, Secretary Jiang Xi, covering five counties: Hengyang, Leiyang, Yongxing, Qiyang, and Changning. (Fourth District) Inspector Yang Xuan, Secretary Zhang Taihu, covering five counties: Liling, Youxian, Chaling, Anren, and Yanling. (Fifth District) Inspector Wu Lunhui, Secretary Ling Zhenhuan, covering five counties: Lingling, Daoxian, Jianghua, Yongming, and Ningyuan. (Sixth District) Inspector Ni Shixin, Secretary Zou Chuanshi, covering five counties: Guiyang, Xintian, Jiahe, Lanshan, and Linwu. (Seventh District) Inspector Wu Fenheng, Secretary Zeng Zhaokai, covering five counties: Huarong, Nanxian, Hanshou, Changde, and Taoyuan. (Eighth District) Inspector Wu Shizhi, Secretary Luo Bohe, covering five counties: Zixing, Chenxian, Guidong, Rucheng, and Yizhang. (Ninth District) Inspector Zhu Wei, Secretary Quan Shen, covering five counties: Wugang, Xinning, Dong'an, Chengbu, and Suining. (Tenth District) Inspector Zhou Shulian, Secretary Chang Jiguang, covering three counties: Shaoyang, Xinhua, and Anren. (Eleventh District) Inspector Li Yuanzhu, Secretary Cai Zuta, covering four counties: Anxiang, Linfeng, Shimen, and Fengxian. (Twelfth District) Inspector Liu Li, Secretary Wu Zhenyu, covering four counties: Qianyang, Huitong, Jingxian, and Tongdao. (Thirteenth District) Inspector Wang Jinglun, Secretary Zhang Qiaosong, covering five counties: Xupu, Chenxi, Guzhang, Luxi, and Yuanling. (Fourteenth District) Inspector Zhou Jinghan, Secretary Yuan Yugen, covering six counties: Yongsui, Qiancheng, Fenghuang, Mayang, Zhijiang, and Huangxian. (Fifteenth District) Inspector Ye Xixu, Secretary Li Dongshan, covering six counties: Dayong, Sangzhi, Cili, Yongshun, Longshan, and Baojing.

Responsibilities

1. In the areas inspected, it is necessary to thoroughly publicize the significance of the prohibition in accordance with the publicity guidelines. 2. Urge the county magistrates to separately prepare registers and take pledges within the time limit, and submit them for review. 3. Inspectors shall review the pledges of various kinds from the county government. If they are not handled completely, they can be corrected nearby. 4. Together with the county magistrate, conduct on-site inspections. In addition to the county magistrate being responsible for enforcing the prohibition order, the inspector should fulfill the responsibility of guidance and supervision. 5. After the opium prohibition period has expired, if there is planting, selling, or transporting, the respective county magistrates should be informed to handle it in accordance with the law. 6. The inspector should report to the authorities at any time whether the county magistrates are fulfilling their duties in handling opium prohibition matters.

Han Fuju Personally Interrogates Li Lechuan

Wooden Ox and Wooden Royal Carriage Are All Displayed in the Provincial Government Hall, Resembling a Theater

Jinan Correspondence: The case of the demon people Li Lechuan and others, captured by the Special Task Force of the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau in Houyingfang a few days ago, had been detained in the prison for more than ten days because Han Fuju was inspecting Jiaodong and had not yet returned to Jinan. Last night, Han returned to Jinan, and this morning (17th), he brought the case to the provincial government for personal interrogation. At around 8:00 AM, the Public Security Bureau escorted the false emperor Li Lechuan, the false earth emperor Fu Binqi, the false empress Song Wangshi, and the carpenter Zhi Huaqing from the prison to the provincial government. Thousands of people lined the streets to watch. When Li and others arrived at the provincial government hall, they trembled in fear, their faces pale. Han's wife, sons, and daughters all came out to watch. During the interrogation, after roll call, the divine ox was carried up, and the clothes in the box and the so-called accompanying royal carriage were displayed one by one. For a moment, the hall was bizarre and colorful, like a theater. According to Li Lechuan's confession, he believed in the Big Dipper Sect and had no ulterior motives. When asked what the strange clothes were for, he confessed that they were for dressing up for the Lantern Festival in the first month. When asked what the divine ox was for, he confessed that it was for display in the ancestral hall. Then, he ordered Li Lechuan and others to be returned to prison to await individual interrogation at a scheduled time. At around 10:00 AM, they were sent back to the Public Security Bureau from the provincial government, and the crowd was even more crowded. (December 17th)

Chiang Kai-shek Orders Ten Provincial Governments to Pay Attention to Investigating and Prohibiting Opium Planting

Hankou Correspondence: The measures for investigating and prohibiting opium planting in the ten provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Hubei, Hunan, Henan, Jiangxi, Fujian, Shaanxi, and Gansu were previously announced by the General Headquarters. On the 16th of this month, General Chiang Kai-shek re-issued the [Precautions for Investigating and Prohibiting Opium Planting] and telegraphed them to the chairmen of the ten provinces, the Pacification Commissioners, the army commanders, and the administrative inspectors, instructing them to comply. The following is a summary:

Telegraphic Order to Various Provinces

To the Chairmen of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Hubei, Hunan, Henan, Jiangxi, Fujian, Shaanxi, and Gansu Provinces, the Pacification Commissioners, the Army Commanders, and the Administrative Inspectors: The measures for investigating and prohibiting opium planting in the ten provinces were previously announced and telegraphed. Now, the precautions for investigating and prohibiting opium planting are issued, hoping that you will comply and instruct your subordinates to comply. Before the special commissioners arrive, the precautions that belong to the special commissioners should be handled by the provincial chairman; those that belong to the commissioners or members should be handled separately by the administrative inspectors and the county magistrates. This is hereby telegraphed. Chiang Kai-shek's seal.

Precautions

(A) Before opium seedlings are planted: 1. The special commissioner, together with the provincial government, prints and distributes vernacular announcements to various counties for widespread posting. 2. The special commissioner publishes a vernacular booklet, which the Department of Civil Affairs orders the counties to distribute to the district offices and educational institutions for separate lectures. 3. The special commissioner, together with the provincial government, appoints commissioners or members to go to various counties to print and distribute a brief notice stating "Strict Prohibition of Opium Planting is Ordered; Violators Will Be Executed" and post it in all villages. 4. The commissioner or member, together with the county magistrate, supervises the district office to hold a large meeting on prohibiting opium planting, inviting representatives from all sectors of the party, government, military, and education to attend, holding open-air lectures or organizing propaganda teams to give separate lectures, and sending people to parade through the villages with announcements and notices, beating gongs and drums. The commissioner or member should personally attend the meeting with the county magistrate in areas where opium has been planted more frequently in the past. 5. The commissioner or member, together with the county magistrate, supervises the district office to instruct the township leaders or Baojia leaders to admonish each household and obtain a pledge stating that if they dare to plant opium, they will accept the death penalty, and submit it to the county government for preservation. For places where it is considered unnecessary to have a pledge, it may be exempted, but it must be submitted to the commissioner and the provincial government for verification. The form of the aforementioned pledge is determined by the Department of Civil Affairs and ordered to be printed and distributed by the counties for use. 6. The commissioner or member conducts spot checks on various districts. If the implementation is ineffective, the district chief shall be punished in consultation with the county. If the county magistrate fails to handle it effectively, it shall be reported secretly to the special commissioner for verification. 7. The commissioner or member reports the work situation on a monthly basis for verification. (B) When opium seedlings are planted: 1. The special commissioner, together with the provincial government, issues a general order to the counties to supervise the district offices to divide the opium planting area in the district into several sections, ordering the township leaders or Baojia leaders in or near the section to patrol in rotation. If opium planting is found, it should be eradicated immediately, the opium seeds confiscated, and the planters sent to court. For desolate areas where there are no township leaders or Baojia leaders to designate, the district chief should send people to patrol. 2. The district chief should assess the diligence of all levels of personnel under his jurisdiction at any time and inspect them personally. Those who fail to perform their duties should be reported to the county for punishment, and the inspection situation should be reported to the county for verification. 3. The county magistrate conducts spot checks on the situation in various districts and reports them to the special commissioner, the provincial government, and the Department of Civil Affairs for investigation and handling, and requests that the district chiefs who fail to perform their duties be punished. 4. The administrative inspector should supervise the handling of various counties and report them for verification. 5. The special commissioner, together with the provincial government, appoints commissioners or members to go to various counties for re-inspection. If the county magistrates, military police, etc. are found to be harboring and conniving, it should be reported secretly to the special commissioner and the provincial government for verification. 6. When the special commissioner receives the aforementioned secret report, he should immediately consult with the military and political leaders of the province for verification, and secretly report to the highest military commander for investigation and approval. (C) When opium seedlings emerge from the soil: 1. The county magistrate supervises the district office to instruct the township leaders or Baojia leaders to inspect the planting areas in their respective sections at any time. If any are found, they should be reported secretly to the district office for eradication immediately, and the planters sent to court. 2. The district chief should inspect the area under his jurisdiction from time to time and report it to the county for verification. If any are found, they should be eradicated immediately, the planters sent to court, and the township leaders and Baojia leaders in charge should be reported to the county for punishment. 3. The county magistrate conducts spot checks on the handling situation in various districts at any time and first ascertains the time when opium seedlings emerge from the soil in the county to the point where they can be identified, and reports it to the special commissioner, the provincial government, and the Department of Civil Affairs for verification. The county magistrate should personally go to various districts for on-site inspection during the inspection period, and report it for verification. If any are found, he should immediately supervise the police force to eradicate them, arrest the offenders and bring them to justice, and request that the personnel at all levels in charge be punished. If it is in a boundary area between two or more counties, it should be inspected jointly. 4. After the county magistrate's on-site inspection, the special commissioner, together with the provincial government, appoints commissioners or members to go to various counties for re-inspection. If any are found, in addition to supervising the eradication and executing the planters by shooting, the county magistrate and personnel at all levels in charge should be reported to the special commissioner for punishment. 5. The commissioner or member may consult with the stationed troops for assistance when necessary. The stationed troops should immediately dispatch teams to assist without delay. 7. If officials, soldiers, police, or teams are found to be harboring and conniving, the commissioner or member should report it secretly to the special commissioner. The special commissioner, together with the military and political leaders, should investigate and verify the facts, and secretly report it to the highest military commander for approval, and all shall be dealt with according to military law. (December 16th)

Letter of Opinion from the League of Nations Engineering Expert on the Plan for the Huai River Project

Guiding the Huai River Is the Primary Problem in Improving China's Economy; Water and Drought Disasters Can Be Avoided After the Completion of the Entire Project

The Huai River project is of great importance to the national economy and the people's livelihood. The Huai River Commission previously drafted a plan for diverting the river to the sea and submitted it to the National Government for approval and record. The National Economic Council also considers the Huai River project to be the primary problem in improving China's economy. In the winter of last year, it invited four League of Nations engineering experts, led by Mr. Haas, the director of the League of Nations Water Conservancy and Communications Section, to inspect the rivers in the Huai River basin for a week, accompanied by Xu Kai, the deputy chief engineer of the Huai River Commission. They also provided opinions on the plan set by the Huai River Commission and made a report. The report of the League of Nations engineering experts to the Economic Council on the plan for the Huai River project is excerpted below for the reference of those who are concerned about the Huai River problem.

The Huai River basin is located between the Yellow River to the north and the Yangtze River to the south, with an area of approximately 270,000 square kilometers. The Huai River originally had its own outlet to the sea. However, between the thirteenth and fourteenth centuries, the Yellow River breached its banks near Kaifeng and seized the drainage route of the Huai River. The Huai River had to find another way out. In 1852 (i.e., the fifth year of the Qing Dynasty's Xianfeng reign), although the Yellow River moved north from Kaifeng, the downstream of the Huai River could not restore its original course due to silt deposition and the high riverbed. Therefore, for hundreds of years, the Huai River has suffered frequent disasters because it does not have a wide and smooth channel to discharge floods.

In order to prevent this disaster, many plans for guiding the Huai River have been proposed in the past, but many of them can be set aside because they are based on insufficient data. Moreover, the limit of the difference between the drought flow and the extreme flood situation of the Huai River has been determined more accurately in recent years. It is also deeply understood that the purpose of guiding the Huai River is not only flood prevention, but also irrigation and navigation. It is deeply felt that the key lies in making full use of the Hongze Lake to store water, so as to obtain all the practical benefits. There is no other method that can be as perfect and effective as this to reduce the maximum discharge of the Hongze Lake downstream and the water disasters it has suffered in the past. At the same time, this method can be used to store water for irrigation and navigation in years when summer rainfall is abnormally reduced. Therefore, the plans that did not know how to use this natural reservoir to obtain such extremely important benefits can also be set aside. In the first phase, the main problem is how the excess floodwater of the Huai River is discharged from the Hongze Lake: 1. Is it to the Yangtze River via the Sanhe River and the Gaobao Lakes to Sanjiangying? Or 2. Is it to a certain river, roughly east, directly leading to the sea? However, with appropriate economic conditions, both methods can be used in later periods, and the situation can still be improved and made safer.

The committee members have studied the engineering plan of the Huai River Commission and the multi-volume documents and materials compiled by it. With the invitation of the National Economic Council, they personally inspected and surveyed the Huai River from a certain point above Huaiyuan to Hongze Lake, and inspected the proposed dam sites near Jiangba, Hongze, and Huaiyin, and inspected many river channels and abandoned river channels. They also traveled south from Huaiyin along the Grand Canal through Gaobao Lake to Shaobo and the Yangtze River. The colleagues did not have the opportunity to meet with Li, the chief engineer of the Huai River Commission, which is regrettable. However, when the colleagues were stationed, Li was handling important projects elsewhere. However, they had a joint discussion with Hui Xukai, the acting chief engineer of the commission, and he provided the necessary explanations. He also accompanied them on a field inspection from Bengbu to the Yangtze River.

The engineering department of the Huai River Commission has conducted detailed research on the terrain of the basin and the records of the water level and submerged areas during the long periods of extremely large floods in 1916 (the fifth year of the Republic of China) and 1921 (the tenth year of the Republic of China). Later, in 1930 (the nineteenth year of the Republic of China), it was decided that the maximum flood volume of the Huai River flowing into Hongze Lake was 15,000 cubic meters per second, which can be fully adopted as the basis for designing flood control projects. After considering the records of the 1931 (the twentieth year of the Republic of China) flood, the colleagues speculated that there was no need to modify the decision. It should be explained that in years of extremely large floods, including 1931, the Huai dikes above Hongze Lake were breached. The aforementioned maximum flood volume was not obtained through direct measurement, but was obtained through various calculation methods. After fully considering the maximum flood volume that can occur after the implementation of the upstream dikes and straight river projects of the Huai River, the colleagues were not entirely satisfied, but in other respects, the calculation method was still appropriate, and the number of 15,000 cubic meters per second was in fact reasonable and sufficient. It is also said that if the maximum flood reaches 15,000 cubic meters per second, according to the records of 1921 (the tenth year of the Republic of China), the flow rate will only exceed 10,000 cubic meters per second for a period of about 30 days.

Based on this assumption, the flood control projects required above the lake should be designed according to the maximum flood volume of 15,000 cubic meters per second, gradually decreasing upstream. However, the gates and dams that control the discharge of water at the lake's outlet should be planned entirely based on the maximum water volume that can be accommodated by the outlet and the downstream drainage channels.

First, regarding the part of the Huai River upstream of Hongze Lake, the Huai River Commission plans to build dikes along the main stem of the Huai River, with a distance of about 3 kilometers to 4 kilometers between the two dikes, straighten several tributaries, and appropriately merge closely adjacent tributaries. The Huai dikes that should be built and extended to the tributaries should also be built. In addition, there should be other ancillary projects to improve navigation and irrigation, which are planned to be implemented later, so there is no need to discuss them in this report. (To be continued)

Kunshan

Imprisonment for Fraudulent Schooling and Extorting Money

Yesterday, three travelers resembling students, Li Qingtang, Zhou Xuexia, and Ren Yuzhi, arrived at the Huaqing Inn in Xuanhua Ward of this county. After renting rooms, they immediately went around soliciting donations, claiming to be establishing a "People's Livelihood School" in Shanghai. Many people donated for a time. The matter was discovered by Qin Jieren, the Director of Public Security, who suspected the affair. He dispatched Officer Zhang Ruofu to lead police to bring Li and the others to the bureau for interrogation. It was determined that they were extorting money under the guise of running a school. They were immediately sent to the county government. After the trial, Zhou and the other person were sentenced to fifty days in prison. Ren Yuzhi was released immediately because he was young and acted blindly.

Wuxi

Farmers in Disaster Area Request Exemption from Arrears Rent

You Wenhuang, Zhang Zifu, You Wenji, and others from Yangmuqiao Township in the Sixth District of this county, stated that their township suffered a flood disaster last year, with houses washed away and fields becoming a sea of water, resulting in no grain harvest. The county government had already verified this and approved landlords to be exempt from national taxes and tenants to be exempt from land rent. Now, with a bountiful autumn harvest this year, farmers and tenants followed the usual practice of paying rent to the granary. However, the granary authorities are forcing them to compensate for the arrears rent from last year, disregarding the certified disaster relief tickets. They have specially petitioned the county government to order the granaries to exempt them from last year's arrears rent based on the disaster relief tickets, in order to relieve the people's distress.

Rice Shop Scion Violently Beats Boatmen

In the river outside the Xin San Fuhexiang Rice Shop outside the North Gate, a covered boat arrived and docked the day before yesterday evening. Unexpectedly, Xu Jinshou and Xu Shuncai, the sons of the rice shop owner, suddenly ordered the boat to leave and forbade it from docking. However, the boatmen, including Gu Xiaowang, had already taken off their clothes and gone to sleep. Seeing that no one came out, Xu became furious and immediately ordered several shop assistants to push the boat away, leading to a dispute with the boatman Gu Xiaowang. They then resorted to violence, giving Xiaowang a severe beating, causing him to collapse on the ground with injuries all over his body. Seeing that they had caused trouble, Xu Jinshou and others scattered. The police officer on duty arrived and arrested two accomplices, Gu Aju and Qian Ajin, and took them to the Fifth Sub-Bureau, while sending the injured person to the Brothers Hospital for treatment. It is reported that his injuries are severe and there is concern for his life.

Changshu

Two Robbers Captured in Yangshuyuan Robbery Case

On the afternoon of January 30th of this year, more than thirty bandits suddenly raided the town of Yangshuyuan in the Fourteenth District of this county, robbing a total of eleven businesses and kidnapping nine people, including Lu Liansheng and Yang Shaoqing. At the same time, the town's stationed water patrol boat, being outnumbered, was also robbed of six rifles and two thousand rounds of ammunition. Officer Li Shihua was wounded by a bullet, and cook Li Shunsheng died from severe injuries. After the incident, the authorities paid extraordinary attention, and the Civil Affairs Department repeatedly ordered the county to cooperate in apprehending the escaped robbers. Subsequently, the Thirteenth Water Police Team successively rescued six kidnapped individuals, including Shen Shuzhou and Weng Zanyang. However, Gu Huiliang, Jing Hongxiang, Jing Hengbao and three others have been missing for nearly a year without any news. Unexpectedly, the other day Jing Ruqiu (the son of the kidnapped Jing Hongxiang) saw two unknown people from other places in a teahouse owned by a person surnamed Shao, who looked very much like the bandits who threatened them with guns at the time. He went to report to his uncle, Jing Yunxiang. After confirming, they secretly reported to the local public security post, which dispatched police to search the teahouse owned by Shao. They captured the two individuals. Shao Yicai, the owner of the teahouse, was also detained on suspicion of harboring bandits. On the 18th, they were escorted to the Public Security Bureau in the city, where the Chief of the Judicial Section conducted a preliminary interrogation. One of them, Tang Guangbin, confessed to running a teahouse in Yu Jing Tang, Wu County. He came to the town to attend the wedding of Lu Guanyun and stayed temporarily at the Shao's teahouse because he couldn't return home. The other, Lu Guanyun, confessed that he was a farmer in Yu Jing Tang and came with Tang to stay temporarily at the Shao's teahouse because he was engaged to a Zhang woman from Yangshuyuan. They claimed to know nothing about the robbery case this spring. The Public Security Bureau, considering the seriousness of the case, transferred them to the county government on the 19th for further investigation.

Qingjiang

Pastry Shops Oppose Business Tax and Go on Strike

There are no less than two hundred and forty to fifty pastry shops inside and outside the city. The Huaiyin Business Tax Collection Bureau has set a deadline for submitting declaration forms to prepare for the collection of business tax from each shop, causing panic among the shop owners. Most of them rely on their small businesses and handicrafts to make a living, and few have capital of around one hundred yuan. If they are also taxed, it will be impossible to bear. Ignoring the tax would lead to fines, so on the morning of the 14th, all the shops went on strike. More than two hundred shop owners gathered at the collection bureau to demand a reduction or exemption, arguing all day without any results. This morning (the 15th), the strike continued. Members of the "Ma" gang workers monitored the "Tu" gang to prevent them from secretly selling food. The "Tu" gang workers, in turn, monitored the pastry shops in Huai'an to prevent them from secretly bringing food. Wu Jiatian of the "Tu" gang secretly sold steamed buns this morning, which was discovered by the "Ma" gang. This led to a large public debt, and the crowd destroyed Wu's shop. Later, the county government and the Public Security Bureau, fearing an accident, sent police to maintain order. Liu Dingxin and others, members of the Standing Committee of the County Chamber of Commerce, came forward to mediate, promising to find a solution for the pastry shops. The shop owners and workers then dispersed and returned to their shops.

The county government recently received an order from the Provincial Finance Department, stating that the amount of taxes collected by various counties was too large, causing people to hide their contracts and not pay taxes. In order to promote tax revenue and reduce the burden on the people, it is approved to reduce the original tax rate by half for one month starting from December 20th. During this one month, the original surcharges and intermediary donations will also be reduced by half. The original overdue penalties will be waived. The county government is now issuing a notice to the public and instructing its subordinates to comply and promote it.

Fortunately, the generals and soldiers of the Northeastern Volunteer Army have resisted with all their might and fought bloody battles for years. However, the generals are fighting for the survival of the people and for the independence of the country, their hard work is meritorious and their names are illustrious, and the whole country admires them and provides support. Our province is far away in the southwest, and the patriotic enthusiasm of the people has not lagged behind. However, due to the poverty of the region, we have been unable to fully support the righteous army, which is regrettable. In addition to collecting a small amount of funds and medicines, which will be remitted separately, we have specially recommended Dou Shaohuai to represent our association and personally go to the war zone outside the customs to comfort them and express our condolences. We should therefore write to your association for verification and request that you contact Dou when he arrives in Shanghai and give him instructions on everything, and that you send a telegram in advance to the generals and soldiers of the Northeastern Volunteer Army for verification. This is our sincere hope.

Yan Bowen's Letter

Yan Bowen, the military commissioner of the Rehe National Anti-Japanese Army and the representative stationed in Shanghai, sent a letter to various support groups yesterday, saying: Sincerely, our army has been resisting Japan for years. The battles, such as breaking Chaoyang, capturing Yixian, seizing Zhangwu, recovering Kangping, occupying Ban Jita, capturing Mengjiatun, attacking Beizhen, and fighting in Jinzhou, etc., have been described in detail in the newspapers and need not be repeated. The capture of Ishimoto and the documents obtained from Honjo detailing the collusion with Chinese traitors to plunder Rehe have allowed Rehe to be preserved to this day. The facts of these military achievements cannot be borrowed by other righteous armies. Furthermore, fighting barefoot in the icy and snowy weather, charging into battle, and rushing through gunfire with unwavering courage are not things that a motley crowd can do. Recently, with the retreat of Su (Bingwen) and Ma (Zhanshan) abroad and the failure and mutilation of the righteous armies (such as Tang Juwu, etc.), the relentless Japanese invaders have concentrated their wolfish forces and are urgently pressing towards Rehe. The mission and responsibility borne by our army are related to the survival of Rehe, the survival of North China, and the survival of the entire China, which is even heavier and greater than before. In general, Su and Ma have become the center of the anti-Japanese movement of the righteous armies outside the customs. If Su and Ma survive, the righteous armies outside the customs can still jointly contain the Japanese invaders and prevent them from driving straight in. If Su and Ma are defeated, the center of the righteous armies outside the customs will be lost, and even if they want to jointly contain the Japanese invaders, it will be impossible. Thus, the Japanese invaders can concentrate on Rehe. Thus, Rehe is in urgent danger. Thus, our army's responsibility and mission to coexist with Rehe is as critical as a hair's breadth. If our army wins, Rehe will not be lost, and the recovery of the territories outside the customs can be slowly achieved. If we lose, the recovery of the territories outside the customs will be even more difficult, and Rehe will also be difficult to protect. If Rehe is not protected, Hebei will be difficult to defend. If Hebei is not defended, the entire North China will inevitably be shaken. Then, Puyi will usurp Beiping, restore the Manchu dynasty, to deal with the powers. The Japanese invaders will then use the navy to press forward, re-enacting the January 28th Incident in the provinces along the Yangtze River, and coerce our government. At that time, our government will be controlled by the Japanese invaders in the south and Puyi in the north. If we want to fight to the death and seek a final victory to avoid the pain of national subjugation, how can it be possible? The importance of our army's responsibility and mission is as described above, so we hope that our army can fight a long-term war and defeat the Japanese invaders. To enable our army to fight a long-term war and have the hope of defeating the Japanese invaders depends on the continuous support of our compatriots in the rear. The replenishment of ammunition, the transportation of cotton clothing, and the preparation of supplies must all be planned by our compatriots in the rear. The mission and responsibility of our compatriots in the rear is more important than that of the soldiers at the front. I think your association is the most powerful group of our compatriots in the rear supporting our righteous army, and all of you are virtuous and courageous heroes who are most enthusiastic about supporting our righteous army. You should be able to deeply understand the responsibility and mission of supporting the rear, and you should be able to sympathize with the difficulties and dangers faced by the soldiers at the front. Therefore, I take the liberty to state the facts directly, hoping that your association will treat all righteous armies equally in terms of support, so that the soldiers at the front can move forward bravely without any worries. Then, when the lost territories are recovered and we celebrate our triumphant return, we will be grateful for your support and acknowledge the merits of your association. Is this not appropriate? As I write, my thoughts are flying, and I cannot express all that I want to say. I specifically write this letter to convey my urgent need for support.

(2) It should be formally announced that the puppet state of Manchuria will not be recognized, and Japan, which created the illegal puppet state of Manchuria by violence, must be severely sanctioned. (3) Japan should be held fully responsible for all the losses suffered by China from the Japanese violent invasion since the September 18th Incident in 1931. (4) It should be proposed to use the pressure of various countries to sanction Japan's illegal acts of destroying peace and invading Chinese territory as a slight punishment. However, the five-nation resolution draft does not mention this point, abandoning its life of fairness. The association is deeply saddened by this and dares to seriously declare to the outside world that the Chinese people will never agree to any resolution that does not adopt the above minimum matters and will resolutely oppose it. We also hope that our people will use their own strength to actively carry out fundamental and effective efforts.

Promoting Trade with Russia

Commerce is prosperous and returning goods are famous. Businessmen of all kinds live prosperous lives. Tracing back to the prosperity of the local business community, trade with Mongolia has always been the only source. Later, due to the independence of Outer Mongolia, Zhangku's business has been greatly affected. Due to the severance of diplomatic relations between China and Russia, Zhangku's trade has been completely cut off. In recent years, the losses of Chinese businessmen's lives and properties in Kulun have been uncountable. The bankruptcies and unemployment of local businessmen from all walks of life are no less than tens of millions. This kind of difficulty is universally known throughout the country, and it is not easy to reverse the situation regarding national diplomacy. Fortunately, in the commercial area of many years, although Outer Mongolia has severed trade, Inner Mongolia and the local area can still operate as usual, and the livelihoods of merchants from various industries can still be barely maintained. However, in recent years, the harshness of national and local taxes and the variety of names have made it impossible for businessmen from all walks of life to bear them, and they have been unable to cope with them. Previously, the various counties jointly launched a movement to eliminate harsh taxes and levies and made requests to all parties, but they have not received any consideration. Appeals for assistance have now been made, but there is no way to appeal. Now, the chambers of commerce of all counties in the province have jointly elected representatives to rush to Nanjing to appeal for relief. Our association has elected two representatives, Cheng Tingmo and Guo Kuizhang, to accompany the representatives from various counties to Beijing to carry out the petition. The representatives are new to Beijing and Shanghai and are unfamiliar with the area, and there are many barriers to all matters. Because merchants are one body and have a common destiny, we believe that the implementation of the request to eliminate harsh taxes and levies and restore Zhangku's trade will be sympathized with and assisted by all of you in your association. In addition to the representatives meeting with high officials to present everything in person, we should write to your association to ask for your love and care, to give you contact and to maintain guidance, and so on. Upon approval, we will investigate that Zhangjiakou is an important route for trade between our country and Outer Mongolia and Russia. The city is prosperous. Since Outer Mongolia became independent and China and Russia severed diplomatic relations, business has been interrupted and the city has declined. In addition to the exploitation of harsh taxes and levies, the number of bankrupt and unemployed merchants is countless. Now that China and Russia have restored diplomatic relations, trade will also develop, and Zhangjiakou's recovery is in sight. However, harsh taxes and levies are a real obstacle to progress. The chamber of commerce and others have experienced the situation firsthand and are in great pain. Now, the province has publicly elected representatives to go to Beijing to petition, and they should send a telegram to the Yuan and Ministry to inspect and verify. Please approve the request and quickly order the Chahar Provincial Government to issue a notice to the entire province to eliminate harsh taxes and levies in order to maintain business difficulties. This is an urgent request. Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce and Industry.

He Bingxian Discusses Sino-Russian Trade Situation

After Resumption of Diplomatic Relations, Commerce Between the Two Countries Should Advance. Cheaper Russian Goods Will Be Beneficial to Our Country. Chinese People Should Adopt a Policy of Promoting National Products.

Following the declaration of resumed diplomatic relations between China and the Soviet Union, the people of both countries have celebrated in unison. This event will not only strengthen the friendship between the two nations but also greatly enhance the economic ties between them. He Bingxian, Director of the International Trade Bureau of the Ministry of Industry, gave a detailed account of the Sino-Soviet trade situation yesterday, which is recorded as follows:

Soviet Russia's Foreign Trade System

Soviet Russia's foreign trade is entirely the exclusive right of the government, which is also a part of the entire system of the Soviet Russia's New Economic Policy. It was legally stipulated on April 22, 1918. The competent authority for this privilege is the People's Committee for Foreign Trade. The actual operators are the national import and export trading companies specially established by the government and the trading companies affiliated to state-owned industrial organizations, as well as other franchised trading companies. People's organizations may not engage in foreign trade without special permission. The main objectives of state-owned enterprises are, firstly, to address the backwardness of Soviet Russia's mechanical industry, which necessitates the absorption of essential industrial construction supplies through state-owned methods; and secondly, to rectify the significant disruptions in the Soviet Russian national economy's distribution, which requires the redistribution of national gains. Therefore, both imports and exports are subject to planned restrictions and systematic planning. On the one hand, this is influenced by the needs of various industries for raw materials, machinery, and equipment; on the other hand, it is guided by the surplus of goods, credit, and the potential for various intangible incomes to offset the deficit of necessary imports. In other words, the state rationalizes foreign trade based on established plans, the degree of need, and the surplus of commodity production.

Current Status of Soviet Russia's Foreign Trade

In 1913, Soviet Russia was still in the era of Imperial Russia, with an annual production value of 20,040 million rubles. After the revolution, it increased year by year, reaching 29.1 billion rubles in 1930 (calculated at pre-war rates), which should be 145.2, an increase of 45%. However, its exports have decreased significantly compared to 1913. The ratio of exports to production in 1913 was 7.6%, while currently it is only 2.9%. This shows the increase in production and the restrictions on exports. Moreover, almost all exports are limited to timber, kerosene, fur, flax, ramie, and grains, accounting for three-fifths of total exports. The main reason is that Soviet Russia has undergone fundamental changes since the revolution. Exporting is not aimed at seeking profitable markets abroad with domestic surplus products but purely at offsetting the deficit of necessary imports. Therefore, the quantity of exports depends on the necessary imports. Before the war, Imperial Russia was an important country for agricultural products in the world (agricultural products accounted for 70% of exports before the war). Now, it is trending towards industrial exports, accounting for 60%.

Trade Situation Between China and the Soviet Union

There have been significant changes in trade between China and the Soviet Union before and after the revolution. It should be noted that China's trade with the Soviet Union is passive, while the Soviet Russia's trade with China is active and entirely controlled by the Soviet Russia's state-owned policy. Before the European War, exports to Russia were worth about 48 million customs taels. Recently, they have increased to 89 million (1928), and in 1930, about 50 million. However, the types of goods have changed. Imports from Russia were previously worth about 20 million customs taels, and they have remained at about this level in recent years. After the resumption of diplomatic relations, trade between the two sides will naturally have significant progress. At the same time, Chinese people are also ordering Russian goods to compensate for the lack of domestic products. Although transportation is affected by the rebellious situation in the Northeast, transportation in Xinjiang, Mongolia, and the Northwest is also convenient. The development of trade can be expected. However, Soviet Russia's foreign trade already has a set policy. Imports are absolutely limited to necessities, and exports are based on the standard of not hindering the national economy. This is not comparable to other countries with freely operated commerce. Therefore, after the resumption of diplomatic relations, the development of trade between the two countries may tend to focus on imports. A large amount of goods such as kerosene, timber, and other commodities that Soviet Russia can sell abroad will be imported, which will benefit our country due to their low prices. However, it is unlikely that exports to Russia will have special and significant achievements. The major export products to Russia were originally beans and tea, but the future of beans this year is unknown due to the rebellious situation. Other products are mostly not necessary for Russia. This can be inferred from the statistics of growth and decline over the years. At this time, if the Chinese people do not pay close attention to the promotion of domestic products, the result may change the surplus of exports over the years into a deficit of imports from Russia. The development of trade may not be as enthusiastically expected by the Chinese people now. In short, the Chinese people should adopt the promotion of national products and the development of industry as a permanent and fundamental policy to seek new outlets in foreign markets, so that we may succeed.

Russian Commercial Representatives Begin Activities

Contacting Our Business Community to Promote Sales

Nanjing dispatch: According to business circles, after the resumption of diplomatic relations between China and Russia, the Russian commercial representatives stationed in Nanjing, Tianjin, Shanghai, and Hankou will openly engage in activities and contact our business community to promote sales. It is expected that after the appointment of ambassadors from both countries, the Russian side will first restore the shipping route between Vladivostok and Shanghai, specializing in the transportation of goods. They will also organize large freight stations and large trading firms in Tianjin and Shanghai. The Russian goods sold in China will mainly include wool textiles, kerosene, hardware materials, woolen cloth, paper, and other miscellaneous goods.

Heavy Fog Obstructs Navigation Yesterday Morning

Gradually Dispersing in the Afternoon, Waterways Gradually Resume

Heavy fog occurred in the local area the night before last. Yesterday morning, maritime traffic was almost completely obstructed. It was not until noon in the afternoon that the weather changed and the fog dissipated. Some of the obstructed ships were able to enter the port. Details are recorded as follows:

Yesterday Morning

The local area was heavily foggy. Around one o'clock in the morning, it was almost impossible to see objects across the street. There were also dense clouds in the Yangtze River basin, and the air pressure was very low. Commercial ships coming to Shanghai from various places were unable to enter the port due to the fog. A total of sea vessels, including Fusheng, Dingsheng, Shengjing, Mankoku, Mikasayama Maru, Katori Maru, Shibade, Fengtian Maru, Yiwenhua, Nafok Maru, and Tai Ma, as well as river vessels such as Tonghe and Wenzhou, temporarily anchored in the waters of Wusongkou to avoid danger. Even European and American mail ships that are never delayed, such as Empress of Russia, Ligee, and President Monroe, failed to arrive in Shanghai yesterday morning. They all telegraphed to extend the import time. From 5:00 AM to 12:00 PM, only three ships, including Jianghe and Xinning Shao, were able to pass.

Afternoon

The weather changed, and a slight northwest wind rose in the outer sea of Wusong. The heavy fog gradually dissipated. Among the ships that had been obstructed, those that had reached Sanjiashui, such as Dingsheng, Taiyuan, Xinming, Fengtian Maru, Tianjin Maru, and British and American mail ships, rushed to Shanghai. After 3:00 PM, Lu Lai sailed into the Huangpu River, but the ship schedule had already been missed. The rest of the ships that did not make it in time will enter the port today. The regular scheduled ships that were delayed were all working overtime last night to load cargo to reduce the time spent in Shanghai so that they could depart as usual today. As for the Shanghai-Ningbo liners, Xin Beijing and Xinning Shao, each ship still sailed out last night, and all the Zhejiang Bay ships also departed.

First Snowfall in the Local Area Yesterday

The weather in the local area has been unusually warm for the past few days, with the Fahrenheit temperature rising to around 70 degrees. Yesterday, suddenly dark clouds covered the sky, and it was unusually gloomy. At about 3:10 PM, snowflakes suddenly began to flutter, with drizzling rain. In an instant, it arrived, and the weather has turned slightly cold. It is feared that there will be heavy snowfall.

City Chamber of Commerce Opposes Stamp Duty on Ship Tickets

Painfully States That It Has No Legal Basis and Requests That It Not Be Misinterpreted and Applied by Analogy

The City Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Executive Yuan and the Ministries of Finance and Communications yesterday, requesting the exemption of stamp duty on ship tickets. The original text reads: Nanjing Executive Yuan, Ministries of Finance and Communications: On the 17th of this month, the Inland River Shipping Industry Association sent a public letter stating that the Jiangsu Shanghai Stamp Tax Bureau issued a notice last month, ordering that from December 1st, all ship passenger tickets worth one yuan or more must have stamps affixed, and dispatched bureau staff to intimidate and force the affixing of stamps, causing the industry's members to be uneasy and requesting an emergency meeting to quickly seek relief. The association held a meeting in winter and unanimously agreed that the stamp duty on ship tickets has no legal basis and is impossible to accept. It was decided to telegraph the Executive Yuan, Ministry of Finance, and Ministry of Communications to promptly issue an order to abolish it. It is noted that stamp duty is a good law implemented in various countries around the world, but ship tickets have never had stamps affixed to them. Even a search of various countries in the East and West reveals no such precedent. Furthermore, the Provisional Measures for Stamp Duty Regulations do not include ship tickets. Therefore, the stamp duty on ship tickets has no legal basis. Secondly, the state must have the Legislature approve and the Executive Yuan promulgate each type of tax law before it can be implemented according to law, but the stamp duty on ship tickets has not gone through the above legal procedures. Therefore, the stamp duty on ship tickets has no legal basis. Thirdly, ship tickets are a transformation of the bamboo slips of the past and are temporary symbols, not comparable to other permanent documents. Therefore, the stamp duty on ship tickets has no legal basis. Fourthly, since ship tickets are temporary symbols used by the transportation industry, with the same nature as train tickets and bus tickets, even if stamp duty is implemented, the ruling party cannot be biased. Therefore, the stamp duty on ship tickets is also not in line with the situation. To sum up, there is no possibility of implementing stamp duty on ship tickets. If implemented, it will not only increase the burden on the people but also violate the Provisional Constitution. Therefore, the details are specifically stated, and it is requested that your office promptly forward them to the Executive Yuan, Ministry of Communications, and Ministry of Finance to issue an order to abolish the imposition of stamp duty. After investigation by the association, it was found that ship passenger tickets, the use of stamps, according to the Stamp Tax Law Interim Regulations Article 2 one to four categories, none of this provision, the Tax Gazette quoted the instructions issued by Your Ministry on September 8th to the Shandong Stamp Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Bureau in the document, the stamp duty law is now being drafted and revised in preparation, should be in accordance with the interim regulations prior to promulgation, do not cite analogies, causing criticism and the letter of August 10th to the Executive Yuan Secretariat, also ordered all provinces of the Stamp Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Bureau strictly order all subordinates, before the promulgation of the Stamp Tax Law, still in accordance with the regulations established case handling, shall not distort and seek, slightly involved in harsh treatment, because ship tickets posted are not expressly provided for, not a reference is distortion, kernel and the above department orders do not conform, should be telegraphed to your office for inspection, prompt correction, it is for the public convenience, Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce bow down to you,

Three-Party Negotiations on the Fuhai Frigate Case

Three-Party Negotiations

Regarding the misunderstanding and gunfire incident between the Fuhai patrol frigate of the Jiangzhe Fisheries Administration and the Jiangnan Shipyard, the shipyard side yesterday telegraphed Navy Minister Chen Shaokuan and sent a letter to the Fisheries Administration for serious negotiations. At the same time, the Fisheries Administration also received a formal report from Guo Wei, the captain of the Fuhai frigate, and reported the situation to Minister of Industry Chen Gongbo, requesting instructions on how to deal with the matter. The details are recorded separately below.

Letter to Fisheries Administration for Negotiations

After the negotiators dispatched by the shipyard were blocked and returned to the shipyard, the shipyard, for the sake of peaceful resolution, sent a letter to the Fisheries Administration for serious negotiations. The original letter stated: I am writing to inform you that the Fuhai of your administration was repaired at our shipyard last year, totaling more than 20,000 taels of silver in repair costs. After repeated requests for payment, the shipyard initially made excuses and then ignored the requests. Yesterday, it was reported that the ship was docked in the Huangpu River, so the shipyard immediately sent personnel on large and small ships to inquire and facilitate negotiations. Unexpectedly, the personnel on the ship opened fire to prevent boarding and negotiations. What is the reason for this? It is difficult to understand. I hope you will investigate and reply promptly for proper handling. This is addressed to the Jiangzhe Fisheries Administration of the Ministry of Industry, Jiangnan Shipyard.

Fuhai Reports the Situation

In addition to receiving a letter from the shipyard, the Fisheries Administration also received a formal report from Guo Wei, the captain of the Fuhai patrol frigate. The report stated: Your subordinate frigate was ordered to set sail to patrol and protect fishing in the Dinghai area. Subsequently, this month, repeated telegrams were received, ordering the frigate to sail to Shanghai to await dispatch. Therefore, on the 14th of this month, the frigate sailed from Shenjiamen to Shanghai and arrived at Tongjiang Bay on the evening of the 15th, docking at Guanhuaigiao to await orders, all of which have been reported. Unexpectedly, at 2:00 PM on the 17th, two armed ships of the Jiangnan Shipyard, Jiangnan Jiangkang, suddenly sailed towards your subordinate frigate. The officers and soldiers of the ships were exposed and prepared to attack. Only when they were one zhang away from your subordinate frigate did they realize that the target of their attack was your subordinate frigate. At that time, the situation was extremely tense. Later, the personnel on the two armed ships remotely shouted, ordering your subordinate frigate to lower its flag and remove its weapons. Judging from their appearance, it seemed that they were planning to plunder the frigate. At that time, your subordinate was not aware of the truth and, moreover, was in the Shanghai area, where military police were everywhere. Therefore, your subordinate only ordered the officers, crew, and sailors to be on strict alert to avoid accidents. Seeing the alert, the two ships circled for about 30 minutes before automatically sailing downstream of the Huangpu River. Your subordinate frigate belongs to the administration of your office and is also part of the government's armed forces. Today, it has unexpectedly been attacked, which is deeply shocking. If it were not for proper precautions, it would have been difficult to avoid being robbed. Therefore, the details of the situation are reported in detail. Guo Wei, Captain of the Fuhai Patrol Frigate.

Report to the Ministry Requesting Instructions

After receiving the official letter from the shipyard and the report from Guo Wei, the captain of the Fuhai frigate, the Acting Director of the Fisheries Administration, Zhou Chengkui, believed that the matter was of great importance and should not be decided arbitrarily. Therefore, yesterday afternoon, he telegraphed Minister Chen of the Ministry of Industry in Nanjing, stating: Recently, your subordinate Guo Wei, the captain of the Fuhai patrol frigate, reported that (omitted details) and other details. While processing the case, the Jiangnan Shipyard also claimed that (omitted details) in order to handle the matter. After reviewing the details, the Jiangnan Shipyard did not first return to the competent authorities for handling but instead took direct action. It is clearly erroneous to ask an officer not in charge to order the frigate to lower its flag and remove its weapons. In addition to ordering the Fuhai frigate to await instructions from the Ministry, the circumstances were reported by telegram for review and handling.

Shipyard Telegram to the Ministry

The Jiangnan Shipyard sent two telegrams to the Ministry of Industry yesterday. (Telegram 1) Minister Chen of the Ministry of Industry in Nanjing: The Fuhai patrol frigate of the Jiangzhe Fisheries Administration of your ministry was repaired at our shipyard last year and completed in November. The repair cost was a total of 20,291 taels of silver, which has not yet been paid. Our shipyard has repeatedly sent letters urging payment, but they have been excused as not being approved by the ministry. Now our shipyard urgently needs this payment to pay the workers' wages. I sincerely request that your ministry order the Fisheries Administration to promptly return the repair cost in full. Thank you very much. Jiangnan Shipyard. (Telegram 2) Minister Chen of the Ministry of Industry in Nanjing: Telegram has been received. The shipyard previously undertook the repair of the Fuhai patrol frigate of the Jiangzhe Fisheries Administration of your ministry, which has now been ten months, but the repair cost has not yet been paid. Please order the Fisheries Administration to promptly return the money to be used for reimbursement and request instructions. Jiangnan Shipyard.

Grain and Silver Transported to Northeast China

Large Quantities of Wheat Flour Purchased in Northeast China

After the Japanese army occupied Northeast China, our ports have blockaded Northeast China's seaports, and the customs have ordered a ban on food grains being carried to Northeast China's seaports, but recently, Northeast China is still procuring large quantities of wheat flour in Shanghai and transporting it to Shenyang and other places. All purchases are shipped to Dalian, and more than 300,000 bags have been purchased and transported. The flour has been shipped one after another, and the last batch was exported today.

Eighth Major Shipment of Funds Sent Out

Since November 6th, Shanghai has begun transporting silver dollars to Shenyang. In these 40 days or so, a total of seven batches have been shipped, and together with the 300 to 400 boxes transported by the Dalian Steamship Company, they have reached more than 20 million yuan. Today, the eighth batch was shipped out by British ships yesterday, amounting to more than 2 million yuan, and will still be transported to Dalian and then to Liaoning. Including the previous seven shipments, the total amount of silver dollars transported is 24 million yuan.
