Jinghu-Huhang section Railway Special Party Committee Executive Committee.

Urgent Seniority Wage Increase, Central Executive Committee: It has been found that the railway department's general order No. 3163 stipulates that seniority wage increases for railway employees, except for special merit, may not be universally granted, which has become a bad example, increases the huge annual burden, fosters the habit of employees seeking advancement, and intends to abolish the precedent of seniority wage increases. Since this order was announced, all employees of the two routes have been extremely agitated, and there is widespread panic, as if a major disaster is about to occur. As a matter of duty, this committee cannot remain silent. Railway employees sacrifice their lifelong efforts and contribute to railway administration, hoping only for this seniority wage increase. If this hope is suddenly dashed, how can they be encouraged to serve loyally? According to the precedent of seniority wage increases, railway employees are entitled to seniority wage increases as their work history and experience increase. Moreover, in the event of death or resignation, new hires are paid at the lowest level, which does not increase the railway bureau's budget. As for those with special merit, there are separate reward measures. Today's order from the railway department not only does not benefit railway administration but also incites employee unrest and creates unprecedented panic on the two routes. It has been found that the railway department has recently arbitrarily added redundant personnel, established agencies, and has been unrestrained, resulting in the railway burden increasing several times annually. If this continues, the railway will inevitably go bankrupt. The railway department's unnecessary waste has only increased, while the seniority wage increase system that examines employees and promotes railway administration is now being canceled, which is particularly infuriating to employees of this route. Because the Shanghai-Hangyong station team members have not yet announced their seniority wage increases for the twenty-first year, they have all gathered and repeatedly petitioned the railway bureau, which promised to respond on the 20th of this month. If a satisfactory solution is not found, the situation will inevitably escalate. I beseech your committee to order the railway department to immediately announce and withdraw the order No. 3163 and maintain the precedent of seniority wage increases on this route. Furthermore, employees in all stations and factories, except for the Shanghai and Songjiang factories, have not been paid, which is extremely unfair, causing employees throughout the route to petition. The cold telegram has been submitted to your office for investigation. I beseech you to strictly order the railway department to immediately order the railway bureau to pay them all to show fairness and avoid accidents. The telegram is sent urgently and awaits orders. Executive Committee of the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway Special Party Department, Council of the Two-Route Unions.

Telegram to All Employees from the Two Railway Unions

Four Expectations for Director Huang

The two railway unions telegraphed: "To all employees of all sections, offices, factories, and stations of the two railways, and to all members of the branch offices: We have recently sent a telegram to Huang Hao, Director of the Railway Administration, which reads: 'To Huang, Director of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou Railways Administration: Since the Japanese invasion of Shanghai, we have suffered greatly. The victims along the entire two railway lines are countless, and the suffering is beyond words. We earnestly hope that the Railway Administration will implement policies to help those affected, so that the employees in distress can soon return to their normal lives. Although the production volume of the railway administration did not decrease significantly even during the war, there have been no commendations to encourage employees after the restoration of peace, despite their loyalty. First, the salary increase policy for employees earning over 100 yuan was suspended. Then, relief loans were divided based on war and non-war zones. Now, even seniority-based salary increases are being cancelled with flimsy excuses. All of these issues, which the previous Director Chen Xinghan failed to resolve satisfactorily, have been brewing and causing unrest throughout the railways. His sudden resignation has left the employees of both railways feeling lost and fearful. We are deeply disappointed. Fortunately, you have been appointed as the new director. We hope that you will quickly implement new policies and show benevolence. Therefore, the hopes that the employees of both railways placed on the previous Director Chen are now transferred to you. We believe that you are already aware of these issues and have good solutions to soothe the anxieties of our employees. We hereby present to you four urgent matters that need to be resolved: (1) The relief funds for the employees of the two railways have been approved by the ministry, but are limited to war zones. However, since the war began, the entire railway line has been affected. Although Shanghai suffered the most severe damage, almost every day for more than a month, Japanese planes bombed the areas along the railway line to disrupt transportation. All employees in various sections and stations risked their lives to transport goods. Their loyalty is self-evident. Moreover, the panic in various ports and the tight market conditions caused untold suffering. Limiting the relief to war zones is unfair to those who faced similar dangers. Therefore, we requested that the relief be distributed without geographical restrictions, but the previous Director Chen failed to find a way to persuade the ministry to make an exception, leading to increasing public anger. This issue must be resolved immediately and cannot be ignored. (2) The salary increase issue for January and July of this year has been properly handled in other sections, but the Shanghai-Hangzhou section's Transportation Department delayed the announcement until November. After repeated requests, the matter was submitted, and the department sent representatives to Shanghai to demand action. The Railway Administration initially promised a decision within ten days, but then stated that the salary increase was being processed when the ministry issued a suspension order, causing the process to be interrupted. This situation is causing concern. It is reasonable to assume that the ministry's suspension order applied to the entire railway after August 1st of this year, but the Shanghai-Hangzhou section's salary increase should have been processed with other sections before the order, and should not be restricted. This is unfair and unreasonable. We request that you address this issue immediately and fairly, and release the salary increases as soon as possible to reassure the employees and maintain stability on the railways. (3) Railway employees sacrifice their lives and work diligently, hoping only for seniority-based salary increases. However, the ministry suddenly issued an order stating that this has become a bad practice and that only those with special merits can receive these increases. The right to seniority-based salary increases involves filling vacancies with the lowest-ranking employees in a cyclical manner, which does not increase the Railway Administration's budget. Special merits should be rewarded separately through medals. Cancelling seniority-based salary increases will not only be detrimental to the railway, but will also make employees feel insecure, causing unprecedented panic. To protect the legal rights of employees, we must request that you immediately submit a request to the ministry to rescind this order and maintain the existing practice of seniority-based salary increases. (4) Railways are national production agencies and cannot be compared to other types of agencies. Since the beginning of the two railways, a bonus has been awarded at the end of the year to show compassion. This bonus comes from 20% of the railway's annual surplus, used to reward hard work and not wasting national funds. Now, there are rumors of cancellation, which will extinguish all hope for employees. If we are not good to them, how can we expect them to work hard? This small expense benefits the people and does no harm to the nation. In this time of anxiety, such inauspicious news is unsettling. Although these are just rumors, we urge you to investigate and prevent them from becoming reality. Please approve and announce the bonuses soon to reassure the employees. The above four points are urgent matters that cannot be delayed. As you have been entrusted with great responsibility and are the hope of the people, we urge you to exert all your strength to resolve these issues immediately and prevent any further accidents. We submit this to you and hope for your wise consideration. We eagerly await your response. The Council of the Railway Unions of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou Railways under the Ministry of Railways.' This is the telegram." The Seal of the Council of the Two Railway Unions.

Continued Records of Kong Xiangxi's Inspection Tour

Further news regarding the inspection tour of Mr. Kong Xiangxi, special envoy for industrial affairs to Europe and America. We have received correspondence from New York, stating that Mr. Kong, along with his entourage, has recently been engaged in propaganda work in New York regarding the Sino-Japanese issue. Over a period of ten days, the American Foreign Policy Association, the Sino-American Association, the Sino-American Cultural Association, the Pacific Association, and the YMCA held meetings and invited him to give lectures. The topics of his lectures were mostly about the Northeast China issue and China's construction plans. After the lectures, discussions were held. It is reported that there was a heated debate at the American Foreign Policy Association. Journalists with extensive knowledge of Eastern affairs, such as Socks and Feffe, were present and strongly sided with Japan. Mr. Kong vehemently refuted their arguments, and his wife and entourage also joined the debate, which was very intense. Socks and Feffe later changed their attitude in their newspaper articles. Important figures from the American Foreign Policy Association, such as Bi, have recently published articles in newspapers advocating that the United States should unite with other countries to impose an economic embargo on Japan. Recently, Chinese and American figures have been secretly active on this matter. Mr. Kong recently gave a lecture at Yale University on the economic issues of Northeast China. He refuted Japan's claim that it needed to occupy Northeast China for economic reasons, using statistics on population, food, and raw materials to argue that Japan's needs were far less urgent than China's. He argued that Japan's invasion of Northeast China was due to the expansionist ambitions of its warlords. The faculty and students of the university greatly appreciated his lecture. Mr. Kong is now planning to establish a permanent propaganda organization in New York, uniting Chinese and foreign figures. The organization is already in place. As for his inspection schedule, it is reported that in mid-November, he visited the Brooklyn sugar refinery, the Baltimore copper and iron factory of Bethelem, and the Colt and Winchester armories in Hartford and New Haven.

Telephone Losses in the Shanghai War

Totaling Over 240,000 Yuan

After the January 28th Shanghai War, the Shanghai Telephone Bureau's telephone projects in Zhabei, Wusong, Zhenru, Nanxiang, and other places were destroyed by Japanese artillery fire, resulting in significant losses. The statistics on these losses were officially released by the bureau yesterday and are detailed below: (Monthly Revenue) The bureau's usual monthly revenue includes 14,000 yuan in monthly rental fees, 6,500 yuan in long-distance telephone fees, 1,000 yuan in Chinese and foreign telephone membership fees, 2,000 yuan in private line fees, and 500 yuan in installation and transfer fees, totaling 24,000 yuan. During the Shanghai War, only 6,000 yuan was received, resulting in a loss of over 18,000 yuan. (Production) Losses in production: 70,000 yuan for the Zhabei branch, 8,000 yuan for the Dingwan branch, 2,000 yuan for the Nanxiang branch, 3,000 yuan for the Wusong branch, 2,000 yuan for long-distance lines, 1,000 yuan for new long-distance projects, 15,000 yuan for wooden poles in inventory, 102,800 yuan for wire rope, 10,000 yuan for building damage, and 5,000 yuan for personal belongings of employees at the Zhabei branch, totaling 218,800 yuan. (Restoration Costs) After the war, the bureau immediately sent personnel to repair the damaged projects to maintain communication. The project cost was initially estimated at 3,000 yuan, but due to the addition of tools and raincoats, it exceeded 2,000 yuan. The total cost of the restoration project for the Zhabei branch and the headquarters was 5,825.28 yuan. The total loss from the above three items is over 242,600 yuan.

Customs to Divide Sections for Cargo Inspection

Starting from New Year's Day

Customs Commissioner Luo Fude of the Jianghai Customs issued Announcement No. 1261 yesterday, stating: "For the purpose of facilitating the inspection of goods on ships that have not yet reached the docks and are moored in the middle of the Huangpu River, the various sections of the port will be temporarily divided into three customs wharves for cargo inspection starting from January 1, 1933: South Wharf: Inspect cargo loaded on ships in Section 2 and above of the port; Customs Wharf: Inspect cargo loaded on ships within Sections 2 to 7 of the port; Lanlu Wharf: Inspect cargo loaded on ships in Section 7 and below of the port. All merchants are hereby notified."

Record of the Annual Meeting of the Chinese Federation

The Chinese Federation held its 20th annual meeting at the association's auditorium at 3 p.m. on the 18th. Those in attendance included Dr. Wu Liande, Xu Jigong, Zhao Yu, Wu Tingpei, Lu Qingliang, Huang Jianzhong, Xu Yuanlong, Wu Jishun, Xu Zhiyan, Qiu Hanping, Situ Shang, Wang Yunyu, Li Guohua, Zhang Xiqi, and over a hundred others. Xu Jigong presided over the meeting, with Yao Zhenlong recording. After the rituals, the chairman reported on the association’s history, stating that the association was founded by Dr. Sun Yat-sen in coordination with overseas Chinese leaders such as Mr. Wu Shirong and Dr. Wu Liande. At that time, the first official chairman was Mr. Wang Jingwei, and the vice-chairman was Mr. Wu Shirong. When Yuan Shikai declared himself emperor, the Chinese Federation increased its opposition, and suffered suppression. The association's affairs were briefly suspended, but soon revived after Yuan's death. Last year, due to a misunderstanding with the party department regarding overseas Chinese affairs, it suffered another setback and almost stopped operating. After clarification, the situation was resolved. The association’s contribution to the revolution cannot be overstated, and we have no regrets in serving our motherland. That is why Sun Yat-sen said, "Overseas Chinese are the mother of the revolution," which shows the importance of overseas Chinese to the revolution of our motherland. Since the January 28th Shanghai Incident, the association has telegraphed overseas Chinese around the world, appealing for economic aid. The amount raised was no less than ten million, but the association did not handle the funds directly, resulting in the creation of the Overseas Chinese National Salvation Economic Committee, with Zhu Qinglan, Zheng Hongnian, and Xu Shiying serving as chairman and vice-chairman, respectively. Later, Zhu Qinglan went to the Northeast, so Xu Shiying and Li Denghui took over as chairman and vice-chairman. At the same time, the association, recognizing the endless aggression of Japanese imperialism, organized the Chinese Federation News Agency to expose their atrocities. In light of the widespread suffering of the refugees after the Shanghai Incident and the lack of medical care for the poor, the Chinese Federation Hospital was established to provide free medical treatment and medicine to the poor and sick. At the same time, recognizing the need for a channel of communication between overseas Chinese and their motherland, the Chinese Federation Bi-Weekly was published. Furthermore, in order to understand the economic life, personal suffering, treatment of overseas Chinese in various countries, and immigration regulations, there was a motivation to establish an Overseas Chinese Cultural Museum. The above represents a brief overview of the association’s work since its revival. As I am old and weak, I hereby announce my resignation at the annual meeting to rest." Dr. Wu Liande then gave a speech, stating that the contribution of overseas Chinese to the Republic of China is already expressed in Sun Yat-sen's words, "Overseas Chinese are the mother of the revolution." We can say that without the financial aid of overseas Chinese, Sun Yat-sen’s revolution and the Republic of China would not have been born, and we would still be under the rule of the Manchus. This is not an exaggeration. The process of establishing the association has already been reported by the chairman, and the details are all true. When I and Mr. Wu and others assisted Dr. Sun Yat-sen in establishing this association, it was to unite overseas Chinese for the great construction of the country. Now, we must continue to strive with the same spirit as before. Since Mr. Xu took office as chairman, he has devoted himself to reorganizing the association, which has been a great contribution. Therefore, I sincerely hope that he will continue to be responsible. Mr. Wu Yingpei then gave a speech, stating that the association was born at the same time as the Republic of China. The details have already been explained by Chairman Xu and Dr. Wu, so there is no need to repeat them. I have a proposal to organize an overseas Chinese club to connect the emotions of overseas Chinese from various places. As for Mr. Xu's resignation, we cannot accept his request. Discussion Items: (1) Organize an overseas Chinese club: Nine preparatory committee members were elected, including Xu Jigong, Wu Yingpei, Wu Jishun, Huang Jianzhong, Qiu Hanping, Wang Yunyu, Wang Guanbin, Zhang Chuming, and Xu Zhiyan, to be convened by Wu Yingpei. (2) Elect three members to review and revise the charter, including Huang Jianzhong, Qiu Hanping, and Wang Zhonglin, to be convened by Huang Jianzhong. (3) Elect seven members to prepare for the re-election, including Xu Jigong, Zhao Yu, Wu Yingpei, Huang Jianzhong, Wang Yunyu, Qiu Hanping, and Wu Jishun, to be convened by Xu Jigong. (4) Xu Jigong's resignation as chairman should be decided after more than 480 overseas organizations have made their selections. Before the selections are made, Xu Jigong will continue to serve as chairman. (5) The assembly unanimously elected Mr. Huang Jianzhong as the general director of the association, but Mr. Huang declined due to business matters and his imminent return to Sumatra in the South Seas. Efforts are still being made to persuade him. (6) It was resolved to hire Chen Wulie as the honorary chairman of the Chinese Federation Hospital and Wu Liande as the honorary director. Finally, the entire group took a photo, and the meeting adjourned at 7 p.m.

Nagasaki Customs Seizes ["Good Luck"] Cigarettes

Due to One and Two Dime Notes Hidden in Cans

According to the Nagasaki Nichinichi Shimbun, passengers traveling to Japan from Shanghai on connecting Chinese ships all carry cigarettes. The customs authorities, due to concerns about the health and habits of passengers, stipulate that each person may carry one hundred cigarettes. Anyone exceeding one hundred cigarettes will have them confiscated. Recently, there have been rumors of valuable items being secretly hidden in Chinese cigarette cans. Therefore, the Nagasaki Customs inspects the cans of Chinese cigarettes brought into Japan by passengers. Unexpectedly, on the morning of the 13th, during a can inspection of fifty "Good Luck" cigarettes produced by the Shanghai Huada Tobacco Company, one and two dime notes from the Central Bank were discovered. Customs officials were quite surprised and considered it a violation of the Customs Law for taxable items. The item was detained. However, while there are relevant regulations for opium and valuables, there are no procedures for dealing with banknotes. Later, after discussions between Anjiang Customs Chief Aoki and Chief Guard Matsuda, it was decided to send the notes to a charitable organization. It was also learned that the Huada Tobacco Company included the notes to promote sales. Therefore, the passenger carrying the cigarettes could not be charged with a crime.

After graduation, they will be assigned to the two roads as road police. National Goods Association Disapproves Zhao Jinji's Membership

The Shanghai National Goods Factory Association sent a letter to various factories yesterday because the Zhao Jinji Thermos Factory falsely claimed to be a member, stating: "On the 13th of this month, major newspapers in this city published an advertisement for the Zhao Jinji Thermos Factory, falsely claiming to be a member of this association. While we were preparing to investigate, we suddenly received Zhao Jinji's application for membership and a letter of recommendation from a member. The association sent personnel to conduct an on-site investigation. The bottle shell was indeed self-made. We then visited the bottle core factory in Yuangeng Lane, Miller Road (which is the bottle core evacuation department, not the bottle core manufacturing factory). We saw three enemies inside. When asked, the factory owner Zhao Jinyuan replied that they were technicians, responsible for evacuation work, earning 2.8 cents per piece, and would not be needed after six months. The investigation report was submitted to the Standing Committee on the 17th, and it was resolved that there was a major suspicion of substitution, and the applicant's membership could not be approved. The false claim of membership will be clarified in the newspaper. This is a matter of record and notification for your information."

Suspicious Person Shot and Arrested

At around 7:00 PM last night, two Chinese police officers, numbers 1020 and 3137, from the Gordon Road Police Station in West Shanghai, were on duty near Xiaoshadu Road and Pudu Road. The area is desolate and has few pedestrians. They caught sight of four people approaching, behaving suspiciously. The two officers stepped forward and ordered them to stop for inspection. Unexpectedly, three of them, upon hearing the order, fled into a side road. One person immediately pulled out a pistol and fired at the officers. Fortunately, they missed. At that time, the two officers returned fire, firing a total of seven shots, six of which hit the person in the head, chest, abdomen, etc. The person collapsed on the road, bleeding profusely. The officers seized a pistol from the person and took it to the police station for filing. The injured person was sent to the Shanghai Municipal Council Hospital by police car for treatment. It is said that the injuries are too serious and the person's life is in danger.

Stablehand Commits Assault on the Road, Chen Gensheng Seriously Injured

At around 3:30 AM yesterday morning, patrolling police officers from the Fifth Precinct of the Fifth District on the Jiangwan Sports Association Road, behind the Central University, discovered a man lying down next to the Shanghai-Songhu Railway west of the Shajing Bridge. They immediately went forward to check. The man was wearing a blue cloth short shirt and pants, white socks, and black shoes. His face was bleeding profusely, and he was barely breathing. The police immediately reported to the precinct and called a car to transport the man to the Tongren Hospital for treatment. After surgery, he became slightly conscious and identified himself as Chen Gensheng, 29 years old, from Jiangyin, residing at No. 111 Yongtai Lane, Gordon Road. He has a wife, Ms. Xu, 27 years old, and a son, Longsheng, who is only nine years old. He had gone from his home to visit relatives on Stablehand Road in Jiangwan the day before. Unexpectedly, when he reached behind the Central University, four or five stablehands suddenly came and violently hacked his head with knives. He fainted from the pain and had no idea what happened afterwards. After learning the details, the lead officer quickly returned to the precinct to report. Chief Dai Hongen secretly ordered the officers to hunt down the murderers. After the case was solved, it was learned that the victim's face had been hacked a total of eight times, with the most serious injuries being one cut to the forehead and two cuts to the back of the head. Therefore, his life is still in danger.

Huang Lianfu Crushed to Death by Machine

Huang Lianfu, a 48-year-old man from Ningbo, was working as a mechanic at the Fuxin Flour Mill on West Suzhou Road. At around 8:00 AM the day before, while oiling the machine, it was still running. He was accidentally crushed severely. People in the factory saw this and, together with Huang's brother-in-law Du Xuezhong, sent Huang to Renji Hospital for treatment, but he died soon after. The hospital reported to the New Police Station, which ordered detectives to investigate and took the body to the Faelun Road Morgue. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Local Court dispatched Prosecutor Zhan Liangce to the morgue to examine the body and record the case. Huang Aipin, the deceased's son, testified that he was 18 years old and that the deceased was his father. He had started working at the factory in May of this year, but he was originally from his hometown, so he did not know the details at the time. Du Xuezhong testified that the deceased was his brother-in-law and that he worked with him in the factory, but he worked upstairs, so he did not witness the event. After obtaining the testimony, Zhan concluded that the deceased Huang Lianfu, male, was indeed crushed to death by the machine before his death. The body was handed over to his son Huang Aipin for burial.

News from Various Native Place Associations

Liu Chongwu of Danyang, motivated by righteous indignation, threw a grenade to warn unscrupulous merchants and was arrested by the police station and prosecuted. The case has not yet been resolved. The Danyang Native Place Association, in order to seek the welfare of its fellow villagers, decided to assist Liu and organized the Liu Case Support Association, pushing Pei Yuanding, Pei Weimin, Pei Weichen, Dong Xiaoqian, Dong Zhenzhi, Han Liangqi, He Binshi, He Qunshang, Ma Yaoxian, Yu Kang, Wang Weixin, and eleven others as committee members. The Support Association held several meetings, all feeling that the case was complicated and difficult to handle immediately. They first sent personnel to investigate the truth of the case and hired lawyer Ma Nangeng as a legal advisor to represent him in court. On the one hand, Yu Kang was pushed to contact various organizations for assistance, and on the other hand, Ma Yaoxian and others were pushed to represent and comfort Liu.

Page 12

On the 11th of this month, this newspaper published a news item entitled "Strange Gunshots on the Telephone." The fact occurred at 11:00 PM on the 10th. At that time, the Zhaizhong Road Police Station in the French Concession suddenly received a strange phone call. The caller spoke urgently, repeatedly asking if it was the police station. The call taker replied that it was, asking where the call was coming from. The caller only replied with the words "French Concession." As soon as the caller finished speaking, two clear gunshots suddenly rang out on the phone, and the call was disconnected. At that time, the head of the police station urgently telegraphed the special agency and notified the various police stations in the Public Concession to do their best to investigate. However, after ten days, nothing was discovered. Only this newspaper exclusively reported the incident the next day and considered it to be bizarre, so it was placed at the top of the page to attract the attention of readers. However, after many days, the truth has never been revealed, which inevitably makes the public suspicious. In view of the importance of this case, the reporter believes that it is necessary to thoroughly investigate and give readers a satisfactory answer. Therefore, the reporter inquired until yesterday, when the reporter encountered a friend from Ningbo who discussed the case of Le Zhenbao, the owner of the Taichang Wood Shop, a large merchant from Ningbo on Nanjing Road, being kidnapped. He felt that the situation was related to the strange gunshots. (The following is all from the friend's words.) Since Le was kidnapped, a month has passed. Initially, the bandits contacted Le's family frequently. Eventually, they reduced the ransom to a minimum of 100,000 yuan. The negotiations were getting closer. Unexpectedly, after the strange gunshots occurred, the bandits disappeared without a trace. The negotiations between the two sides suddenly broke off. At that time, Le's family speculated that the bandits' hideout was probably equipped with a telephone. The hostage, when everyone was quiet at night, managed to call the police station, hoping to be rescued. Unfortunately, the bandits noticed it and shot him. This is also a possible fact. Now Le's family is extremely grief-stricken. On the one hand, they are actively investigating, hoping that this speculation is not true. Even if Le was unfortunately killed by the bandits, they must at least find the remains. After listening to the friend's words, the reporter felt that the facts were not contradictory and the situation was quite consistent. This is recorded to see what happens later.

Zhu Tieying Wrongfully Drowned at Sea

Only Able to Sacrifice the Small Self for the Public Good

The Facts are Clear, No More Groaning

Zhu Tieying, the editor of the Taicang Moye Newspaper, after being sentenced to three months in prison by the local court for defamation, wrote to his friend Mr. Hu from the detention center yesterday due to family economic constraints, saying that he would not appeal again. However, Zhu's friends are all urging Zhu to appeal again and fight for justice. It is said that Zhu must wait for the court's judgment to be served before deciding whether to appeal. The original letter to his friend was extremely painful. It is recorded below. (Above omitted) "After receiving the letter, I can understand that you are disappointed. However, although it does not require travel expenses to appeal to the High Court, it only requires a written statement, but it often delays the process for at least three months. My wife and children rely on me for their livelihood, and the affairs of the newspaper need me to manage them, and the economy needs me to adjust. If I extend it for another three months, my family will have unspeakable pain. What's more, it's like fighting a stone with an egg, and evil forces permeate the entire society. What justice exists in this world? What's more, the defamation law is the most vague. My heart is really unwilling, but I can only endure it. Therefore, after careful consideration, considering my environment and identity, I can only sacrifice the small self for the public good and not appeal again. Then, after 30 more days of hardship in the detention center, at the latest by the end of the lunar year, I can regain my freedom. I also know very well that it is ten thousand times more painful in the detention center than outside. I am still trying to find a way to struggle. Please ask my wife to come forward and tell you in detail. I don't want to bother anyone else to rescue me. I can only submit. After I am released, I will express my great gratitude to everyone who rescued me. Now, I can only ask you to bother Mr. Zhang once more and ask him to write a letter of withdrawal of the appeal. This procedure cannot be avoided, so as not to have to return to the detention center for the five days of sacrifice. Then, it is estimated that I can be released from prison after December 23rd or 24th of the lunar calendar and have a good meeting with you. This time, you have done your best to rescue me. The results are as follows. The tragic words of the weak can only be attributed to fate. However, the facts are clear, and there is no need to make meaningless moaning. With this, I respectfully wish you well. Your younger brother, Zhu Tieying."

Unfilial Son

Actually Threatens Mother with Cleaver

The Police Request a Severe Punishment

The Old Mother Is Fond of Her Son

Requests the Judge Not to Reduce the Sentence

Tao Luo, an old woman from Chongming, is 65 years old. She lives in a bungalow with no number on Yangshupu Road. She has a son named Heshang, who is 28 years old, does not engage in honest work, and only associates with vagrants, indulging in gambling and pleasure-seeking. His mother often scolds him, but her admonitions are met with abuse. She only has this one son and can do nothing but sigh and weep all day long. A month ago, the mother slightly rebuked him for something, and Heshang wanted to strike her with his fists. After the neighbors persuaded him to stop, at around 6 PM the day before yesterday, Heshang gambled outside and lost, returning home with anger in his chest. The mother slightly questioned him, and he began to roar, grabbed a cleaver, and threatened his mother. The mother was terrified and fled out the door, screaming for help. Just as Hua Tan Liu Changgen heard the alarm and arrived, he questioned the situation and immediately arrested Tao Heshang, took him to the Yangshupu Police Station, reported to the head of the police, and ordered him to be detained. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Summary Court of the First Special District. Police lawyer Qian Xunjiu stated the facts of the case, and filed a public prosecution on the crime of harming a close relative under the second item of Article 293 of the Criminal Law, requesting a severe punishment. Then, Officer Liu reported the incident again, but the old woman Tao Luo still doted on her son, asking the court to give him a slight punishment, sentencing him to one month's detention, etc. When questioned, the defendant bowed his head in silence and asked for leniency. Judge Zhang Junqing sentenced Tao Heshang to 30 days of detention as a warning.

Robbery

Li Heji Wooden Workshop: At No. 8 Kuaijia Lane, Jiuxiaochang, Chengnan, the Li Heji Redwood Workshop opened by local resident Li Housheng, was suddenly attacked by five local-sounding robbers at around 9 PM the day before yesterday. One of the robbers was a woman in a blue cheongsam, with five pistols hidden in her chest. They first lurked at the entrance of the Li family to guard and stopped pedestrians from entering. The robbers then obtained pistols from the female robber and went straight to the Li residence. They also went to the home of Su Jinrong, who set up a vegetarian chicken stall at the City God Temple, and used pistols to intimidate them. They then went to the Li's inner room and used a hatchet to break open the redwood glass cabinet and leather suitcase, and stole two gold lockets, one gold chain, four gold rings, two gold buttons, one gold bracelet, two men's leather robes, and one black wool coat. Afterwards, the victim reported to Xu Chenghuang, the chief of the second precinct of the first district, who sent police to pursue the robbers, but they had already escaped. The case has been reported to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for pursuit.

Chunfeng Pawnshop: The Chunfeng Pawnshop at No. 124, west of XX Lane, Caishi Street, French Concession, is an old shop that has been around for many years. The counter is equipped with iron fences. Usually, every day around 10 AM, when the vegetable stalls close, the shop sends clerks to buy small silver coins from the vegetable stalls, which is a common practice. Yesterday (the 19th) at 10:05 AM, two robbers, one wearing a copper basin on his head, wearing a blue serge shirt and pants, speaking with a northern accent, and about 30 years old, each armed with a pistol, one guarded at the door, and the other took advantage of the pawnshop clerk's departure to buy small coins, and broke into the shop, holding a gun to intimidate the counter staff and preventing them from making a sound. They immediately grabbed 63 yuan and 120 small coins from the counter drawer, opened the fence and fled. Afterwards, the manager of the pawnshop reported the situation to the Dada Ziminzhong Police Station and requested an arrest.

Letter

To the Editor: I read in your newspaper on the 15th of this month an article stating that unscrupulous merchants in the electrical appliance industry were selling enemy goods, and that the National Products Maintenance Association had sent a letter to your newspaper to advise our association. After investigation, our association has not received any letter from the association. It is feared that someone is borrowing the name of patriotism to try to damage the reputation of our association. In addition to sending a letter to the association to inquire about the truth, we are afraid of confusing the public, and we should ask your newspaper to make a correction. Sincerely, Shanghai Electrical Appliance Industry Association, December 19th.

Reader Advice

(1) Discussion on the Question Raised by Mr. Bao Zhizheng

|| Original letter seen in this column on the 17th of this month

Mr. Xu Gengsheng's message: After reading the letter, we only feel boundless indignation accumulating in our hearts, wanting to burst out. | Is it not right to ban fortune-telling, astrology, witchcraft, geomancy? But there is only a text on banning, after the banning, what [legitimate occupation] are they engaged in? Where [factories established locally] are they invested in? How [to make them bear the corresponding work]? These are all big things, and it will not be successful if we do not start from the root; but when will the root of the matter be realized? This is one. Secondly, those who are fortune-tellers and astrologers have already realized and [are willing to change careers], but the [Public Security Bureau] [orders them to continue business as usual], which is nothing less than [the world's strange talk]? It turns out that the [wives and young masters] of these [officials] need [them to pray for them] when they have [diseases]; therefore, although the Jiangsu Provincial Government has [seven banning measures], the [Public Security Bureau] still [orders them to continue business as usual]. Not enough [orders], more need [obligation], not enough [obligation], plus [all kinds of extortion], [grabbing] [black fees], all these kinds of things make it difficult for us to understand what world it is today? Although, these are all digressions, in my opinion, if you are not willing to be subjected to this [dark] [coercion], the only [new way out] is to [resist] it without hesitation. You can unite your [ninety] or so [companies] and jointly submit it to the Jiangsu Provincial Government and the Supervisory Yuan, asking them to thoroughly investigate and deal with it. I think [the authorities] still hope that politics will be clarified, and they will definitely give considerable punishment to this kind of [black] [Public Security Bureau]. Secondly, there is the issue of future occupations. Since there are no factories in your place, this layer is indeed extremely difficult, but since the banning measures clearly stipulate a time limit, it seems that you can gradually change careers separately within the stipulated time limit, so that you will not feel sudden and unprepared. If a lot of time has been delayed due to the [order] of the Public Security Bureau, you can also explain the reasons and apply to the competent authorities for an extension. As for the industry to be changed, there is no certainty. Those who are physically strong can engage in agriculture, those who are better in writing can fill in the records, and the rest can all be merchants, but blind people have a problem. In short, a sudden reform will inevitably have considerable difficulties. Wait a few days, and everything will not be a problem. Fortunately, you and your colleagues should not worry about the difficulty of changing careers. A temporary pain can be exchanged for endless hope in the future.

(2) Mr. Gu Runsheng's message: I am an 18-year-old youth who graduated from junior high school this year during the summer vacation. My original intention was to continue my studies, but my grandfather did not agree. Because he is running a shop in XX and the business is not bad. But my father always doesn't care about things and smokes opium at home all day long. My grandfather's intention is to have me help him in his shop. He said that going to school is just that, and now I should practice as soon as possible, and I will be the successor in the future. But I think that my grandfather is still working hard (he is now in his sixties), and the economy is still relatively well-off. I can take this opportunity to discuss my further studies. Besides, I am now very young, and I have no clue about the ways of the world, human feelings, business conditions, and accounts. Even if I sit in the shop all day, I can't help him. It's really not good for everyone. So I talked to the old man several times. He didn't agree at first, and then when he got anxious, he said that I was young and didn't understand things and didn't love to improve. Sir, don't you think this is wrong? ...

Now there is nothing else to say. Although I have been imprisoned in the shop by the old man, my idea of going to school has not been dispelled. Sir, please teach me a way!

[Answer] This magazine deeply sympathizes with your eagerness to improve. Your grandfather's opinion may seem [outdated] to young people, but it also has its reasons. Presumably, your grandfather's current career is the result of his lifelong hard work. He certainly has no deep belief in the knowledge of books. In addition, many school graduates now often disappoint the elders; of course, his opinion is different from yours. Originally, book knowledge and practical experience are complementary. . Knowledge without experience is floating knowledge; experience without knowledge is narrow experience. Today's school education mostly focuses less on practice and more on theory, which is to seek knowledge while ignoring experience; so going to school does not necessarily achieve the desired result; no wonder people doubt it. For example, you think that now [you have no clue about the ways of the world, human feelings, business conditions, and accounts], so you want to go to school, but even after graduating from university, [you are afraid that you will still have no clue about the ways of the world], even if [business conditions and accounts] are seen in books, but what is recorded in the books is only the essentials, and the real situation in the business world is still ever-changing, making people [have no clue]. Moreover, your grandfather does not want you to take charge alone now, but only to [practice]. This is a great opportunity. Since you are eager to improve, you may as well study on your own in your spare time. In this way, you will link the experience you have gained with the knowledge in the books, and what you gain in half a year will definitely match the achievements of one year in school, or be more practical. Don't over-believe in school education and miss a good opportunity.

Jiangsu Province School Teachers and Staff Representatives' Request for Funds Has Made Some Progress

Representatives Confer with the Education Fund Management Office

Method of Issuing Two and a Half to Three and a Half Months

Yesterday's Petition to Zhenjiang

More than 30 representatives from various schools of the Jiangsu Provincial Middle School Teachers' Association Provisional Plenipotentiary Representative Assembly went to the Education Fee Management Office at 7:00 PM on the 17th to discuss funding issues with Director Niu and Section Chief Liu of the office. As reported yesterday, the two sides exchanged opinions until after 10:00 PM, resulting in the following decisions: The funding notice for the second half of August will be filled out and issued on October 9th of this year, with a deadline of the 25th of this month. Funds can be withdrawn from the bank upon expiration. The Medical Examination Committee will sign and issue funding notices for September and October on the 25th of this month. The deadline for the September document is January 15th, with funds available for withdrawal from the bank upon expiration. The October document will be filled out in two installments: one on January 20th and the other on January 25th, with funds available for withdrawal from the bank upon expiration (the above refers to receiving cash). For November funding, it was decided that county and township teachers' colleges and experimental primary schools will continue to follow the old practice of advance payment. Schools will either go to the respective counties to withdraw funds or negotiate with the Finance Department to order the counties to raise funds as a substitute for the counties to repay the outstanding educational expenses to the province. The issuance of the (November) payment notice will either be filled out and issued on the 25th of this month or wait until the beginning of next month. This will be determined after Section Chief Yang returns to Nanjing after urging payment. Regarding urging the provincial government to repay the accumulated outstanding provincial education funds (before the division in the 19th year of the Republic, a total of more than 1.9 million was owed; after the division, 700,000 was owed; in the 19th and 20th years, 365,000 was owed in provincial subsidies, totaling nearly 3 million), if collected, it would be enough to cover one year's worth of education expenses in Jiangsu Province. Therefore, the root cause of the accumulated educational fees in Jiangsu Province does not lie in the Management Office, but in the Finance Department, and not in the Finance Department, but in the misappropriation by various county and bureau affiliated to the Finance Department. It is reported that the Songjiang Finance Bureau reported that only 20,000 was owed in education fees, but after the Management Office sent Section Chief Yang Zishen to audit the accounts, it was found that the amount should be more than 60,000. Such concealment is not limited to one county. The Management Office is currently trying to rectify this situation. Accordingly, the representatives held a meeting at the Management Office and unanimously decided that each school represented at the meeting should send at least one representative (those with two or three or more representatives from each school in this session should still go as a principle, unless there are special matters), totaling several dozens of people, to go to Zhenjiang with the section chief of the Management Office on the morning of the 19th to urge the provincial government for payment. The 18th was a Sunday. In the afternoon at 6:00 PM, Niu Tixsheng hosted a banquet for the school representatives at Jinlingchun, and Section Chief Yang Zishen reported on the situation of urging payment and discussed the method of issuing two and a half to three and a half months' worth of funding. The next day, the entire group went to Zhenjiang.

Recommendations from the League of Nations Education Survey Team

Preliminary Plan for Reforming Chinese Education (Part 1)

Necessary Efficient School Administration, Teacher Profession, and School System

At the request of the Chinese government, the League of Nations Administrative Council commissioned an expert education survey team from the International Cultural Cooperation Society to come to China to conduct surveys in order to improve the Chinese education system and facilitate cultural exchange between China and foreign countries. The team consisted of four members: 1. Professor Becker of the University of Berlin, former Prussian Minister of Education; 2. Professor Falska, Director of Elementary Education of the Polish Ministry of Education; 3. Professor Langevin of the University of France; 4. Professor Tawney of the London School of Economics and Political Science. They arrived in Shanghai on September 30th of last year and conducted surveys in China for more than three months. The places they visited included Shanghai, Nanjing, Tianjin, Beijing, Dingxian, Hangzhou, Wuxi, Suzhou, Zhenjiang, Guangzhou, etc. After returning to their countries in the spring of this year, they compiled an English report entitled "The Improvement of Chinese Education." After the book was sent to the Ministry of Education in Nanjing, the Ministry ordered editors to translate it into Chinese. It took a month to translate the original book. On the 16th of this month, the National Economic Commission rushed to print 200 copies and distributed them to relevant parties for reference. It is said that the Ministry of Education believes that the report has made a great contribution to the improvement of Chinese education and plans to print and sell it as a separate volume in the future. The original report is divided into two parts: the first part is a general discussion of the situation of Chinese education, the administrative system, and the current school system, with severe criticisms and suggestions in each chapter; the second part discusses primary, secondary, and university education, with detailed criticisms and suggestions on educational standards and methods. The original book contains more than 100,000 words. Due to the limitations of space, this newspaper now records its conclusion, "Preliminary Plan for Reforming Chinese Education," as follows for the reference of researchers.

Preliminary Plan for Reforming Chinese Education The education system of a country is the strongest link in national unity. This has always been recognized in China. However, the recent development under various foreign influences has seriously endangered the unity of national culture. Therefore, the beginning of our proposal is to rebuild this unity under the current changing situation in China and emphasize the national and social nature of the Chinese education system. To achieve this goal, it is necessary to build:

㈠ An efficient school administration to introduce and manage modern education. The main conditions for this establishment are: A. Consolidate the authority and power of the Minister of Education. 1. Expand the scope of action, especially regarding the power of appointment (the main personnel of the affiliated education departments should be appointed by the Minister after consultation with the local authorities or based on the recommendations of the local authorities). 2. People who have a relationship with education (such as special committees and advisory meetings at all levels of administration, retired officials, appointed and publicly elected representatives of teachers and staff, parents of children, and the public) should elect representatives to assist the Minister. B. Unified administration. The three levels of the Ministry of Education, provincial education departments, and county education bureaus constitute an administrative unit. The upper level often governs the lower level, and their powers are stipulated separately, but they are interconnected in terms of administration and finance. Higher education is governed by the Education Department, while elementary education is governed by the county education bureaus.

㈡ An efficient teacher profession A. Teacher training must be reformed. All teachers in the country should be subject to a uniform standard prescribed by the state, and it is recommended that the state conduct teacher examinations, starting with secondary school teacher examinations, followed by the rest. B. The salaries of teachers at all levels should be stipulated according to a certain grade and paid on time. The lack of job security for teachers is the main reason for the current instability and reduced efficiency of the teaching profession. The number of university chairs and teacher positions should be fixed, but they must be stable. The appointment of teachers should be based entirely on qualifications, and dismissal should only be allowed in cases of proven incompetence or for disciplinary purposes. Teachers should be appointed by the主管敎育機關, not by the principal.

㈢ An efficient school system A. To build a truly efficient education system for the whole country, elementary education must be compulsory. The goal should be six years of compulsory education, but the current four years of compulsory education can also be recognized due to local circumstances. Since compulsory education is implemented, elementary education must be free. All children who enter school should not pay fees. Elementary schools are the foundation of the entire system. Under the current situation, the development of Chinese elementary schools is crucial. The implementation of compulsory education must be carefully prepared based on on-site investigations in pilot cities and counties. Because elementary education is fundamentally important, the National Government and the provinces should allocate funds for this purpose. The Ministry of Education should establish a special Elementary Education Department. Also, if the number of students taught by each teacher and each school is increased, there is still room for further improvement in the efficiency of school and teacher utilization.

Junior High School Curriculum Standards (10)

History I. Objectives

(1) To study the evolution of the Chinese nation, especially to explain its historical glory and the experiences of aggression suffered by foreign powers in modern times and their causes, so as to inspire students' thoughts of national rejuvenation and cultivate their spirit of self-confidence, self-awareness, development, and amplification.

(2) To narrate the general situation of the evolution of Chinese culture, especially to explain its contributions to world culture, so as to enable students to understand the great deeds of our ancestors and cultivate their lofty ideals and the spirit of self-improvement.

(3) To narrate the general situation of the history of various countries, explain the characteristics of their cultures, so as to cultivate students' general knowledge of the world, and pay special attention to the origins of the current international situation and the position of our country, so as to awaken students' awareness of their responsibilities in the national movement of our country.

(4) To narrate the changes in Chinese and foreign cultures in various eras, special explanation should be given to the origins of modern political systems and economic conditions, so as to establish students' beliefs in the Three Principles of the People.

II. Time Allocation

Two hours per semester, a total of twelve hours for three years.

III. Textbook Outline

(1) First Year: National History

(1) Ancient History 1. Legends of ancient times, 2. The establishment of the Chinese nation, 3. The politics and education of the Tang, Yu, Xia, and Shang dynasties, 4. Ancient cultures and societies, 5. The establishment of the Zhou dynasty and its politics and education, 6. The Spring and Autumn and Warring States periods, 7. General social conditions of the Zhou dynasty, 8. Schools of thought in the Spring and Autumn and Warring States periods, 9. Conclusion of this period.

(2) Medieval History 1. The unification of the Qin dynasty and the expansion of monarchy, 2. General political situation of the Han dynasties, 3. The opening of the Western Regions and foreign transportation in the Han dynasties, 4. Scholarship and religion of the Han dynasties, 5. General social situation of the Han dynasties, 6. The division of the Three Kingdoms and the unification of the Jin dynasty, 7. The new integration of the Chinese nation, 8. General cultural and social situation of the Jin and Southern and Northern dynasties, 9. The unification of the Sui dynasty and the general political situation of the Tang dynasty, 12. Scholarship and art of the Sui and Tang dynasties, 11. General political situation of the Sui and Tang dynasties, 12. Scholarship and art of the Sui and Tang dynasties, 13. Society and religion of the Sui and Tang dynasties, 14. The eastward spread of Chinese culture, 15. The decline of the Tang dynasty and the chaos of the Five Dynasties, 16. The Song dynasty, 18. Scholarship, thought, and general social situation of the Song dynasty, 19. The military achievements of the Yuan dynasty, 20. The westward spread of Chinese culture, 21. The internal affairs and foreign affairs of the Ming dynasty, 22. The colonization of the Chinese nation, 23. General cultural and social situation of the Yuan and Ming dynasties, 24. Conclusion of this period.

(2) Second Year (Continuing National History)

(1) Modern History 1. The gradual increase in Sino-Western traffic and the introduction of Western affairs, 2. The rise of the Qing dynasty, 3. The politics and military achievements of the early Qing dynasty, 4. The expansion of the Chinese nation, 5. The foreign policy of the early Qing dynasty and the politics of the mid-Qing dynasty, 6. The Opium War, 7. The Taiping Heavenly Kingdom, 8. The Anglo-French Allied Forces and Sino-Russian negotiations, 9. The Sino-French War and the loss of Southwestern borders, 10. The Sino-Japanese War and the pressure of foreign forces, 11. The beginning and end of the Reform Movement, 12. The Boxer Rebellion, 13. The Russo-Japanese War and Northeast immigration, 14. The political system of the Qing dynasty and the constitutional movement in its final years, 15. The cultural and social situation of the Qing dynasty, 16. The economic situation of the Qing dynasty, 17. Conclusion of this period.

(2) Contemporary History 1. Mr. Sun Yat-sen and the revolutionary movement, 2. The Xinhai Revolution and the establishment of the Republic of China, 3. The diplomacy of the early Republic of China, 4. Reactionary politics and warlord melee, 5. Diplomacy after the European War, 6. The course of the National Revolution, 7. The internal affairs and diplomacy after the establishment of the National Government, 8. The most recent cultural, economic, and social situation, 9. Conclusion of this period.

(3) Conclusion 1. The relationship between history and human life, 2. The gradual formation of the Chinese nation and the current rejuvenation movement, 3. The evolution of Chinese culture and its glory, 4. The position of our country in the current international situation.

(3) Third Year (Foreign History)

(1) Ancient History 1. The ancient civilizations of Africa, 2. The development of the Greek nation, 3. Greek culture, 4. Roman politics, 5. Roman culture, 6. India and Buddhism, 7. Conclusion of this period.

(2) Medieval History 1. The opening of Korea and Japan, 2. The migration of European nations, 3. The rise of Christianity and the development of ecclesiastical power, 4. Europe in the feudal era, 5. The founding of Islam and the Arab Empire, 6. The conflict between Christianity and Islam, 7. The westward expedition of the Yuan people and the establishment of the Turkish Empire, 8. Conclusion of this period.

(3) Modern History 1. The European Renaissance and the Reformation, 2. European colonization of the world, 3. The formation of various European powers, 4. The independence of the United States, 5. The cultural and social situation of Europe in the eighteenth century, 6. The French Revolution and its influence, 7. The construction of Germany and Italy, 8. The Industrial Revolution and its influence, 9. The invasion of Asia and Africa by imperialism, 10. The Japanese Restoration and the development of its national power, 11. Conclusion of this period.

(4) Contemporary History 1. The international situation before World War I, 2. World War I and the collapse of the German and Austrian Empires, 3. The Paris Peace Conference and the League of Nations, 4. The Russian Revolution and the establishment of the Soviet Union, 5. The revival of Turkey and the liberation of the world's weak and small nations, 6. The international situation after World War I, 7. The situation in the Far East after World War I, 8. Modern culture and social conditions, 9. Conclusion of this period.

(5) Synthesis 1. The relationship between foreign history and national history, 2. A comparison of foreign cultures and Chinese culture, 3. The responsibility of the Chinese nation to the world.

County Education Bureau Education Fee Audit Committee Established Yesterday

And Held Its First Regular Meeting

The Education Funding Audit Committee of the Shanghai County Education Bureau has been reorganized and held its inaugural meeting at the bureau at 2:00 PM yesterday, followed by the first regular meeting. Attendees included Yu Fen (replaced by Jiang Zhizhen) of the county government, Yang Huiming (replaced by Zheng Yi) of the county education bureau, Peng Liren (replaced by Jin Zuobin) of the administrative committee, Dai Zuyao and Weng Zhuoying of county schools, and Zhang Yi of social education agencies. Jiang Zhizhen was elected as the temporary chairman, and formalities were observed. First, the chairman reported on the reorganization process, followed by discussion of: (1) The resolution to determine the chairman of the committee: Peng Liren was elected as chairman. (2) The resolution to set the date for the regular meetings of the committee: once a month on the 16th, postponed if it falls on a holiday. (3) The resolution to stipulate the audit method: (A) Compare five types of books: vouchers, cash receipts and disbursements, classified ledger, income and expenditure reconciliation table, and income and expenditure calculation sheet. (B) Recurrent expenses should be paid on a monthly average and should not exceed the budget; temporary expenses should be paid annually and should not exceed the budget. (4) Audit results: The income and expenditure accounts were audited and found to be correct, but for the compulsory education portion, receipts returned for supplementation from various schools such as Zigang, Ziyu, Libin, and Juzao, as well as the expense receipts from various people's schools in the first district of the social education portion, should be collected by the bureau within a limited time and submitted to the next session of the committee for verification and pasted into the register. The meeting adjourned after the audit.

Shanghai University Federation Telegraphs the Third Plenary Session

Do Not Restrict Private Individuals from Establishing Universities and Liberal Arts Departments

The Shanghai University Federation held a temporary executive committee meeting at Jiaoyuan on Avenue Road yesterday afternoon. Those present included Zhang Shouyong, Hu Qibing, and Zhu Shijun from Guanghua University, Wang Yuxiang from Daxia University, Yu Nanqiu, Wen Chongxin, and Zhang Yi from Fudan University, Li Yingzha and Hu Duanxing from Jiaotong University, Liu Zhanen from Shanghai University, Xu Peikun from Shanghai Business College, and Yang Yufen from Jinan University. The meeting was chaired by Zhang Shouyong and recorded by Zhang Yi. The chairman reported that the temporary meeting was convened because the content of the "Reform of Higher Education Plan" proposed by the Central Organization Committee of the Third Plenary Session, as reported in the newspapers yesterday, was extremely important and related to the education system and the cultivation of talent. He asked everyone to discuss it as much as possible in order to gather opinions and present them to the central authorities for reference. Subsequently, the representatives discussed it repeatedly for a long time and all agreed that it was necessary to state opinions on the first and seventh items in the original proposal. It was then decided that Shanghai University, Fudan University, and Daxia University should immediately draft a telegram to the Third Plenary Session, the Central Political Conference, the Ministry of Education, and other institutions. Chu Minyi and Wang Bo were publicly recommended to present the case to the Third Plenary Session, and Wang Yuxiang and Zhang Yi were recommended to go to Beijing to handle everything. The text of the telegram is found below:

To the gentlemen of the Third Plenary Session, Mr. Cai Yuanpei: The reform of the education system proposed by the Central Organization Committee in this Third Plenary Session proposes that all universities in the country should be established by the Ministry of Education and that all provincial and municipal governments, bodies, and private individuals should not be allowed to establish liberal arts colleges. Those that have already been established should be merged into state-run schools or ordered to close down. This case will certainly be rejected after discussion by the general assembly. However, for the sake of Chinese education, this association cannot remain silent. To stipulate that all universities in the country be established by the Ministry of Education is a violation of educational principles and the precedents of European and American countries. In fact, the central government has no financial resources to shoulder this responsibility. Looking at the state-run schools that already exist, the government is already experiencing various difficulties in the annual maintenance fees. Today, China's education policy should promote production and practicality, but liberal arts are also necessary for training citizens and developing culture. How can we abandon food because of choking? Looking at the number of university students in our country today, less than one in ten thousand people has the opportunity to enter university, which is already too narrow. In this budding period, the government should do its best to promote it. If it is said that the content is not perfect, there are many ways to guide improvement. It is definitely not the responsibility of the government to promote education by closing schools. The establishment of various private universities has been decades for the old and nearly ten years for the recent. Private individuals have worked hard to create the rudimentary foundation of today. Those who propose the proposal do not cultivate what has already been established, but want to use the name of reform to carry out destruction. It is difficult to understand in terms of reason and difficult to solve. The pillars of the party-state and the advanced education workers can carefully consider the pros and cons and consider everything in detail, so that a ray of life for national education will not be interrupted by this. Please ask the gentlemen of the general assembly to reject the proposal immediately. The future of the party-state is fortunate, and national education is fortunate. Shanghai University Federation bowed.

National Jinan University Board of Directors

Please Urge the Government to Promptly Allocate One Million in Arrears

Return Nanjing School Site, Move Middle School Department to Beijing

Build Library, Gymnasium, and Nanyang Museum

Raise One Million in Funds to Develop Natural Sciences

National Jinan University, founded at the end of the Qing Dynasty, is the only educational institution for overseas Chinese. After this national crisis, it is urgently seeking to improve. During this recovery, a large-scale library, gymnasium, and Nanyang Museum will be built for research. However, the school has no foundation, and the Ministry of Education has accumulated more than one million in fees over the years. Not only is expansion impossible, but maintenance is also difficult. It is reported that the school took advantage of the absence of various directors of the Third Plenary Session on the afternoon of the 17th, except for Chen Yaoyuan, who was still abroad, and Song Ziwen, who was absent due to business. It is estimated that those present included Lin Sen, Sun Ke, Wu Tiecheng, Ma Chaojun, Chen Lifu, Yu Jintang, and兼校長 Zheng Hongnian, totaling seven people. Lin Sen presided over the meeting. The resolutions are as follows: (1) Request the Ministry of Education to promptly allocate more than one million yuan in arrears and increase the budget for operating expenses in installments in order to carry out the revitalization plan and amortize old debts. (2) Request the Ministry of Education to forward a request to the government to return the Nanjing school site so that the middle school department can be moved to Beijing. (3) When the government allocates the arrears, a library, gymnasium, and Nanyang Museum should be built separately, and the library should be rebuilt first. (4) Raise one million yuan in funds, with emphasis on developing natural science.

Municipal Education Bureau

Educational Quarterly, Issue 4 - Call for Submissions

The Shanghai Education Bureau's Educational Quarterly has already published three issues, with rich content. It is a rare publication for the Shanghai education community. It is now heard that the fourth issue is about to be published. In addition to articles on educational theory, it will also include more practical improvement directions and plans for Shanghai education. With publication imminent, those with relevant manuscripts should submit them as soon as possible for consideration. Here are the guidelines for submissions: ㈠ The theme of this issue should focus on improving Shanghai education. Plans for improving Shanghai school education, social education, or other aspects are highly welcome. ㈡ In addition to the above manuscripts, research on educational theory or concrete school plans may also be considered for publication. ㈢ Submissions can be in classical or vernacular Chinese, but must be clearly written and punctuated. ㈣ Submissions will not be returned, regardless of whether they are published, unless they are over 3,000 words and include sufficient postage. ㈤ The bureau reserves the right to modify submissions. Please indicate in advance if you do not wish for your submission to be modified. ㈥ Once a submission is published, a cash reward will be provided, approximately three yuan per thousand words. ㈦ Submissions should be sent to the Compilation Section of the Third Department of the Education Bureau.

New Publication of Famous Sports Works

Practical Massage and Corrective Gymnastics

Written by American Massage Therapist Hartvig Nissen

Translated by Sports Experts Chen Kuisheng and Jin Zhaojun

The [Sports Series] published by the Diligence Bookstore, opposite the National Sports Promotion Association on Father Luo Shen Road, Shanghai, already has more than 30 titles and is popular throughout the country. Today, [Practical Massage and Corrective Gymnastics] is published. The book was originally compiled by Hartvig Nissen, a highly renowned expert in massage and corrective gymnastics, based on his 45 years of research experience and practice. It is considered a highly valuable work in the American medical and sports communities. The translators, Jin Zhaojun, professor of physical education at the Central University, and Chen Kuisheng, physical education instructor at the Hunan Provincial First Normal School, translated it because they saw the lack of such specialized scientific books in China, and wanted to provide it for research, reference, and practical use by the Chinese people. The translators have used the translated manuscript four times in the Yueyun School of Hunan and the Department of Physical Education of the National Central University. All medical, pharmaceutical, physiological, anatomical, and action terms in the original book have been translated into Chinese with reference. The greatest contribution of this book is that in addition to correcting posture and treating injuries, various surgeries and movements can often achieve special effects on diseases of the nervous system, digestive system, circulatory system, and muscle system that are not easily treated by ordinary medicine. It is truly the gospel of treatment and the savior of patients. The entire book has more than 200,000 words and more than 100 illustrations. It is a must-have textbook for universities and physical education departments studying specialized sports books. Printed on Daolin paper, hardcover, priced at 2.90 yuan, special price 10% off. Mail order postage registration fee, plus 16 cents.

New York Stock Market Mixed

A report from the New Asia Foreign Firm states that on Saturday last week (the 17th), the New York stock market was initially strong at the open, but then due to the favorable outlook on the beer case, Coca-Cola was hit, and the market situation weakened again. The number of railway cars totaled 521,216, a decrease of 26,245 from the previous week. The half-day trading volume totaled 414,000 shares. Looking at the current stock market, the situation may not undergo significant changes for the time being, as the stakes in various political and commercial issues are still difficult to estimate. On the one hand, investors will not easily sell, and on the other hand, due to the unstable political situation and the lack of significant progress in industry and commerce, they are also unwilling to buy in large quantities. Therefore, it is expected that the current stock market will not undergo major changes. The closing prices for the 17th are listed on the left:

Yarn and Cotton Sales Suddenly Decline

Rumors of Telegrams from Yunnan and Guangdong Banning Shipments

The yarn market has suddenly fallen, and the situation is turning soft. Actual demand is increasingly stagnant. There are rumors of telegrams from Guangdong and Yunnan banning shipments, and reports state that the Japanese army's shelling in Jehol is severe, leading to public discouragement. However, ordinary retail investors still have a strong desire to go long.

Cotton Standard Drops by One Liang, Five or Six Qian

The cotton standard market opened strong in the morning, following the price of foreign cotton. Unexpectedly, there was a sudden drop in the second and third sessions, causing market panic. Due to the sluggishness and lack of activity in the spot yarn business, prices for all months fell by one liang to one liang, one, two, three, and four qian. The market continued to weaken in the afternoon, with prices for all months falling by two, three, four, and five qian. The total trading volume for the day was 51,300 bales. It was found that Lai sold 1,700 bales from Meiji, 1,100 bales from Xiesheng, 900 bales from Zhenda, 800 bales from Senkang, and 1,050 bales from Tongfu, while Jifeng bought 1,100 bales, Gengfeng bought 1,550 bales, Changyu bought 1,300 bales, Yichang bought 1,050 bales, and Lichang bought 900 bales. The closing prices are listed below:

Spot Yarn Drops by Five Qian to One Liang

Spot yarn sales suddenly declined, and prices fell by five qian to one liang. Total purchases by various gangs for the day were 555 bales (there were also 1,000 bales of standard yarn opened by Yichang, a peer, for hedging). Shenxin Factory opened 1,080 bales of futures and spot yarn, and Dafeng Factory opened 50 bales of balloon yarn. The purchase amounts for each gang are listed below:

Hankou 100 Ningbo 18 Changsha 60 Xuzhou 20

Xiamen 1 Guangdong 10 Inland 57 Luzhou 5

Wuhu 20 Peers 1060 Jiangxi 100

Cotton Drops Six and a Half Qian This Month

The cotton market has plummeted, but the market sentiment is still strong, as most cotton merchants are inclined to buy in because: 1) domestic production is not abundant; 2) sources from all regions are depleted, and inventories are too low; 3) the recent situation of American cotton is relatively stable; 4) the amount thrown out by a certain manufacturer this month is too large, and the delivery of goods each month is particularly lacking. Due to these factors, speculators are vying to buy in, and the desire to go long is quite strong. Therefore, the market is more expensive than the yarn market. It is said that a certain manufacturer is searching for and shipping large quantities of cotton from Tianjin and Shandong to Shanghai.

Zheng Standard Retail Investors Close Positions

The Zheng Standard market opened strong in the morning, with tight conditions due to the short squeeze in the current month. Retail investors were unable to cover their positions, and prices for distant months fell slightly. In the second session, the price for the current month fell sharply. There were many rumors in the market that a certain manufacturer had purchased about 4,000 pieces of coarse cotton in Tianjin, Shandong, and other places and shipped them to Shanghai. Therefore, retail investors closed their positions, and the market plummeted like a bolt from the blue, suddenly falling five and a half qian and breaking through the three liang mark. However, buyers for distant months remained firm and did not let go (there is also a rumor that several brokerage firms purchased a huge amount of 70,000 dan on behalf of a certain foreign firm). Therefore, the bullish side became more and more assertive, with near-term prices falling four and a half to six qian and distant-term prices falling one and a half to two qian. In the afternoon, the price for the current month fell by five fen, the price for the middle month rose by five fen, and the price for the distant month remained unchanged. The total trading volume for the day was 173,300 dan. It was found that Lai sold 14,600 dan from Yuanxingchang, 2,800 dan from Tonghe, 4,200 dan from Shenchang, 2,300 dan from Rongxing, 3,300 dan from Dafeng, and 3,200 dan from Gengfeng, while Shenxinchun bought 7,200 dan, Gengfeng bought 13,500 dan, Ruida bought 4,100 dan, Yuanda bought 7,200 dan, Weihe bought 4,700 dan, Changfeng bought 3,700 dan, and Jifeng bought 3,400 dan. The market prices are listed below:

Statistics on Sales of Japanese Cotton Yarn in Shanghai in November

Sales of cotton yarn by Japanese yarn mills in Shanghai were very strong in November, with a total of over 35,700 bales sold, an increase of 16,449 bales compared to October. This is the reason for the reduction in inventories. The sales volume in various regions is recorded below:

Indian and British Cotton Industry Weekly Report

(Bombay) Market conditions remained tight and stable last week due to short covering. Japanese merchants are improving Balarusi cotton to replace Oomra. The east was quiet until recently when a well-known Japanese merchant suddenly became active. Arrivals are delayed, and the amount of cotton thrown on the market is insufficient. In addition, the gold earned from sales in Upper India can prevent cotton farmers from rushing to sell their cotton. Therefore, market conditions can continue to be strong. Spot demand has improved slightly. Local factories are urgently purchasing for immediate use. The weekly statistics are appended below (units in thousands of bales):
